The author of this book has completed it for you, O sons, with regard to the part of science in medicine which is contained in it and its clarity and simplicity. I have attained the ultimate goal therein by my description and explanation thereof. I have therefore seen fit to complete it for you through this chapter which is a practical application by hand.
For in our land and at this time, when practical skill is lacking, almost to the point of being nonexistent, let alone being taught or its effect being cut off. And the only remnants of it that remain in the early books are rough sketches which have been smudged by the hand and disfigured with errors and obscurities, to the point where their meaning is obscured and their usefulness has been lost.
So I saw fit to revive it and compose in this chapter, by way of explanation, elucidation, and condensation, and to bring together the figures of surgical instruments and all the tools for working with them, as this is an increase in clarity and a fulfillment of what is necessary.
The reason why there is no skilled practitioner of surgery in our time, for the craft of medicine is long and its practitioner should first become well-versed in the science of anatomy which Galen has described. Until he is able to understand the functions and repairs of organs, their healthy and unhealthy conditions, and their connections and disconnections; the number and locations of bones, nerves, and muscles; and the places where arteries and veins branch out.
Therefore Apollonius said, "Physicians are many by name but few in deed, and especially when it comes to the craft of handwork," and we have mentioned some examples of this in the introduction to this book.
For he who is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding anatomy will inevitably make mistakes and kill people thereby, as I have seen many who claimed to be skilled in this art without knowledge or understanding.
And how I saw a foolish doctor cut into a goiter on the neck of a woman, so that he severed some of the ligaments and the woman's blood flowed until she died in his hands.
I saw another doctor who had been successful in removing a stone from a man who had been stabbed in the scrotum, and it was large so he cut into a part of the bladder to remove it. The man died after three days, and I had been summoned to remove it, and when I saw the stone from the bladder and the condition of the patient, I realized that he would have not lived.
I saw another doctor who was a mountebank among some travelling merchants in our country.
I told a black boy who had a break in his leg near the heel with an open wound, and the doctor quickly but ignorantly pulled the fracture on top of the wound with bandages tightly fastened and left no breathing room for it.
Then he let him go, and told him to wait for a few days and not untie the bandage until his leg and foot became swollen, and thus supervising his demise.
So I was summoned to him, and I quickly untied the bandage and he found relief from his pain and eased from his suffering, but corruption had taken hold of the limb and I could not reverse it.
So the corruption continued to spread in the limb until he died.
I saw another doctor who gave him an iron ball that ulcerated after a few days until it became swollen for his owner, and this is because if cancer was pure from blacksmithing then one should not expose him to iron at all.
But rather when there is an organ that may have to be completely excised.
So, my son, you should know that the work of the hand is divided into two parts: a work that ensures safety and a work that causes damage in most cases.
And I have warned everywhere in this book the work that contains deceit and fear, so you should warn yourselves and reject it.
If the ignorant person does not find the way to probing and cutting, take care of yourselves with firmness and protection and be gentle with your patients.
And use the best way leading to safety and praiseworthy outcomes, and tackle difficult and stubborn diseases.
And be cautious about yourselves from what you fear may bring you into suspicion in your religion and world, for it is more lasting for your dignity and higher in this world and the next for your destiny.
For Galen said in some of his sayings, do not treat a bad illness so that you be called bad doctors.
And this chapter has been divided into three gates.
The First Gate.
In the cauterization by fire and in the hot medicinal treatment, which is a swift and an arranged matter from ancient times, and the images of the instruments for cauterization, and the preparations for it, and everything that is needed for the work with the hand.
The Second Gate.
In the incision and the cut and the venesection and the cupping and the surgery and extracting arrows, and similar matters, all of it is a swift and an arranged matter, and images of the instruments.
The Third Gate.
In the lithotomy and the amputation and the treatment of the cataract, and similar matters, a swift and an arranged matter from ancient times, and images of the instruments.
The First Gate.
In Cauterization.
And before we mention its use, it is necessary to mention its advantages and disadvantages, and in what temperament it is used.
And I say that the discussion of the manner in which cauterization is beneficial and its disadvantages is a long discourse and a subtle science, and a secret known to a group of wise men.
And they disagreed about it, and I have shortened the little that I said from their words, out of fear of lengthening.
And I say that aloeswood is beneficial in general for all bad temperaments whether accompanied by a material or not, except two temperaments: the hot temperament without a material and the cold temperament without a material.
And as for the cold temperament with a material, they have differed in it. Some of them said that aloeswood is beneficial in it, while others contradicted them saying that aloeswood does not cure a disease which results from heat and coldness because the nature of fire is heat and coldness.
And it is unlikely that someone with a hot and cold disease would be cured by a hot and cold medicine. And he who contradicted said that aloeswood burned with fire could benefit someone with a hot and cold disease in the bodies of people. Because when you mixed the body's moisture into the fiery temperament, the human body became cool.
And I say that because experience has shown me this many times, unless it should be supposed by one who has been accustomed and trained in the art of aloeswood. And he took into consideration the difference of temperaments among people, as well as the nature of diseases themselves and their causes and symptoms and duration.
And as for the other temperaments, there is no fear from them, especially the cold and moist diseases; all physicians have agreed on their benefit with aloeswood and they have not differed about it.
And know, my son, that whoever knows the secret of treatment with aloeswood burned by fire and its superiority over the aloeswood burned by the burning medicine is that the fire is a single essence which does not exceed the action of the organ it burns nor harms another connected part except for slight harm.
And the aloeswood burned by the burning medicine may exceed its action to what is beyond the parts and perhaps it will cause a disease that makes treatment difficult, or even kill. And the fire, for its dignity and noble essence, does not do this except if it has been excessive.
It has become clear to us through experience in the length of service and care in craftsmanship and establishing the facts of the matter.
So I have dispensed with lengthy speech, but if not for the fact that it does not befit this book, I would have informed you in secret of a subtle method and its manner of doing so to bodies and repelling diseases by philosophical words and proofs that strike at understanding.
Know, my sons, that they have disagreed about the time period which is suitable for bloodletting and have considered the best time to be during spring.
And I say that bloodletting can be beneficial in any time period, because the harm caused by time takes a benefit to cure it which is brought about by bloodletting. And especially if the bloodletting is from a necessary and strong cause that cannot be delayed, lest it follows with biliousness which is greater than the progressing internal harm caused by time.
And do not let it occur to you, my sons, that the bloodletting which cures a certain disease will never recur and make it imperceptible.
And it is not your opinion that the bloodletting is merely a medicinal treatment which tempers the temperament and dries the moistures that are the cause of the pains.
But bloodletting is preferred over medication by its speed of success, strength of effect and intensity of power.
And the disease may return at a time, according to the temperament of the patient and his ability and strength and what is prepared in his body from the gathering of superfluities within him and his neglect towards acquiring it through food and similar causes.
God forbid that the disease for which bloodletting is used be a mild disease with little superfluity and moisture in the member. Similar to the extraction of a tooth due to pain and similar cases, it may not return with that pain, at least.
And as for the common people saying that tooth extraction is the ultimate medicine, it is a correct statement. Not what they claim because they believe there is no remedy that benefits with a drug or otherwise after the occurrence of tooth extraction and the matter is different from that.
And the meaning of "tooth extraction is the ultimate medicine" is that we have tried all types of treatment for a certain disease and those treatments did not work, then if we finally try tooth extraction it works, what benefit or sense is there in saying that tooth extraction is the ultimate medicine. No, by the meaning which the common people and most of the ignorant physicians have gone to.
And the first ones have mentioned that tooth extraction with gold is better than with iron and they said that because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its purity and they said it does not pollute the place of the tooth and that is not at all.
Because I have tried that and found that it does that in some teeth but not in others and extracting with it is better and more excellent than iron as they said, but you if you heat the tool in fire made of gold you will not know when to take it out of the flame so it may burn.
Because it quickly becomes cold and if you increase its heat in the fire it melts down, and you become stuck in that, so because of this extracting with iron has become faster and closer to the truth for us, God willing.
And I have treated this chapter on tooth extraction in sections that I have organized from head to foot so it may be easy for the student who wants it, God willing.
The First Section.
In the tooth of the head, there is one extraction method.
This ointment is useful against the oppression of humidity and cold on the brain, which are causes of headache and frequent falls from the head to the eyes and ears, and excessive sleepiness and toothache and throat pain. And in general for all illnesses that are caused by coldness such as paralysis, epilepsy, and stupor and similar diseases.
A picture of this ointment is that the physician first orders purging with a gentle and refined medication for the head three nights or four, according to the strength of the physician's power, his age, and his habit.
Then he orders him to shave his head with a razor, then sit him before you reclining, having placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your finger on the tip of his nose between his eyes, and where you extend your middle finger make that spot with the ink.
Then take the olive oil vessel shown in this picture.
Strip as much from the bone as a hawthorn or a hazelnut, then lift your hand; otherwise return your hand with the same file or another if it has become cold. Until you see from the bone what I have mentioned to you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water, let him drink a draught of it, put a cotton swab on the place, and leave it for three days.
Then put a cotton swab soaked in grease on him until the itchiness goes away from the fire, then treat him with the quadruple ointment until he is healed, God willing.
And they said that if the wound remains open it will discharge pus and this is better and more useful.
And some of them mentioned that the skin should be cauterized onto the bone and hold the iron until it burns a part of the thickness of the bone, then scrape off what has been burned from the bone, then treat.
They say that one should over-cure it so that it has a strong effect on the bone until it falls from the bone like a small bead or a pebble. And they claimed that steam rises from that place and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then he cures it until it heals. I do not see these two kinds of cauterization except in some people, and by a trick and leaving it is better with safety if so, the head swells when its natural connection is disrupted as we have seen in all other organs.
And especially when the patient's head is weak by nature. The first type of cauterization has pleased me and I have found it better, so if you want to try it then do so, may God grant success.
The Second Chapter.
Also in cauterizing the head.
If something has happened to the majority of the head and there is a chronic pain that persists with the patient and you have used poultices, lint, oil clays, and bandages especially if he was cauterized with one type which we described but it did not benefit him in any way then look. Chapter Three.
In case of the fractured femur that is not chronic.
If there occurs in the fractured skull, with pain and headache extending to the eye, then let the surgeon purge the head with cleansing remedies, and apply all other treatments mentioned for fractures. If this does not succeed, then place a bandage on both sides of the face. Either by applying a hot remedy or with iron.
And as for the treatment with a hot remedy, it is to take one clove of garlic, peel it and cut its edges on both sides, then make an incision in the affected area from the temple using a wide probe until there is space under the skin that can accommodate the clove.
It is inserted under the skin until it disappears, then a strong bandage is tied tightly on top of it and left for fifteen days, after which it is removed and the garlic is taken out. The wound is left to heal for two or three days, then the patient can move about.
And on it a thread dipped in oil is placed until the wound becomes infected, then it is treated with ointment until it heals by God's will. And if you wish, do this using some of the hot remedies I mentioned in chapter eighteen of the hot remedies.
And as for treating it with iron, it is on this form: secure the metal wedge shown in its image.
And it is called the mizmar wedge because its head is like a mizmar reed with some curvature, and in the middle of it there is a small hook.
Then place it on the affected area and hold your hand as you turn the file a little, a little until the amount of skin that burns is like half of it. And lift your hand so as not to burn the artery below and bleeding occurs, then dip a thread in salt water and place it on the area and leave it for three days. Then carry the thread with fat, then treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing.
And if you want to cut this tendinous part with a sharp edge coming from the hook and protect it from cutting of the artery in this non-chronic tendon especially.
The Fourth Chapter.
In a chronic tendinous swelling.
If you treated the swelling with what we have mentioned of treatment and what we have mentioned in divisions of diseases, and the treatment did not cure it, and you saw that the cause cannot be remedied by what we first mentioned of medicine or treatment by fire. It should be that you hold the sharp hook until it whitens after learning its place on the site of pain with a line equal to half a finger or so, and leave your hand once and then pull it until you cut the artery and reach near the bone.
Unless you be careful from the connection of the jaw which moves upon chewing, to burn the muscle or the motor nerve in it so that contraction occurs.
And be on guard and beware of bleeding from the cut artery, for in cutting it is danger. And especially to one who does not know what is done and has not been a tried path, and leaving the work first.
And the treatment of bleeding from the artery will be mentioned in its place in the book, God willing. If you see that the cause cannot be remedied by this treatment.
And if you see that the patient's body is swollen, then introduce a poultice of the caustic in the middle of the head as we have described and treat the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you want to use the caustic which we mentioned in the chapter of cutting the artery with the hook having sharp edges, for it is a better and safer caustic than this one.
The fifth chapter.
For swelling of the ears.
If there occurs an ailment in the ear due to cold and heat, having been treated with poultices and all the treatment that we mentioned in the division and the pain has not gone away, then apply the cautery which is called the spot which this drawing shows.
Then burn it around the ear all over, as it turns round or around both if the pain is in both. And a little above the origin of the ear, lightly after the place has been learned with ink, the cauterizing should be for about ten spots in each ear or near it then treat the places until they heal if God wills.
The sixth chapter.
For the treatment of fistulas.
The fistula which is treated with cautery, is only that kind which occurs from phlegm, as I mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
And one avoids cautery for the kind which occurs from the folds and tension of the nerve.
When you have treated this kind of fistula with alum, vinegar and caustic alkali and the treatment has not succeeded, then it is necessary to recauterize the patient with three cauteries. One at the origin of the ear, and the second a little below the cheekbone, and the third at the joining of the lips.
And make your cautery from against the side which is sick, because relaxation occurs in the side that appears healthy.
The drawing of the cautery, to cauterize it at the tip of the upper ear against the crown of the head a little, and the other on the cheekbone and its length is as long as the eyebrow.
You lower your hand with the cautery until it burns to the depth of half a skin thickness, and this is the drawing of the cautery and it is one of the iron caustics which we mentioned its picture earlier but it is a little softer than that as you see. It is desirable that the needle be somewhat thicker, then treat the place as mentioned previously until it heals by the will of God.
Chapter Seven.
For chronic fistula.
If you treat the fistula by excision and as mentioned, but your treatment is unsuccessful and there is no fever, apply four dressings. On every crown of his head a dressing, and a dressing in the middle of the head as mentioned before, and a dressing on the back of the head as previously described.
The recipe for the poultice as before, and it may also be applied a dressing on the mouth of the stomach which will be more effective, then treat as mentioned previously.
Chapter Eight.
For forgetfulness (amnesia).
The one who is from phlegm it is necessary to give the patient first of big and purified grains for the brain.
Then he should shave his entire head and put on the back of it a poultice of ginger as mentioned in the chapter on dropsy, carrying it repeatedly because it is a remedy.
And do the same on his back in exactly the order as mentioned there, for that is a purifier; otherwise apply three dressings on the back of his head, to be arranged from the top of the head down to the neck.
Make between each dressing a thickness of the width of a finger, then treat the dressings as mentioned before; if you want to increase and the patient is capable of that, apply the middle dressing.
If you want to increase it, apply on the crowns then treat it until he heals, and the poultice will be olive-like in its form as previously mentioned.
Chapter Nine.
For apoplexy and relaxation of all the body.
It is necessary to proceed in the cleansing of the head with aloe-vervum and what we have mentioned, then shave the head of the patient, then sprinkle kohl on the middle of the head and on every horn of the head and behind it.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck, if the disease required relaxation of the body more than that and the patient was capable of it and the disease was strong and tight then sprinkle kohl four times on the vertebrae of his back. And continue to sprinkle the kohl until it burns most of the skin, then raise your hand and treat him as has been mentioned before until he is cured, if Allah wills, and the poultice be dark green.
The Tenth Chapter.
On Convulsions.
It is only the epileptic who has been convulsed previously by phlegm, it is necessary that his brain be cleansed first with big aloe-vervum and all the treatment which we have mentioned in the division if the patient is great and capable of taking medications.
As for him if he is a child and cannot take the medication, he should be treated with the cleaning vessels and the clean digestive substance for the brain before that for many days along with improving his diet.
Then have him shaved and sprinkle one kohl on the middle of the head as mentioned in the condition and another kohl behind it. And on every horn of his head a kohl, if the patient is strong and capable then sprinkle the kohl which we mentioned for the epileptic person and relaxation of the body on vertebrae of the neck and back vertebrae, and the poultice be dark green as mentioned before.
If the patient is a child then make the poultice soft in this shape.
The Eleventh Chapter.
On the treatment of Dementia.
If the cause of paralysis is foul moisture and thick phlegm, administer to him the remedies that we have mentioned for one suffering from epilepsy.
If the cause of paralysis is a weakness leaning towards blackness, and the body of the patient is wet and foul-smelling, cleanse his brain as mentioned in the treatment.
Then shave the head of the patient, then make a tight cake from flax like a disc, and place it in the middle of his head. The patient will sit up raised, holding himself on all sides. Then take one pound of old goat fat.
Then heat it on the fire with moderate warmth, until you can bear to put your finger into it. Then pour it over the middle of his head in the circle and leave it until it cools down. You do this treatment for the patient every week, along with his good management, until he is cured, if God wills.
And if you wish to improve it, pour a great many small quantities of the fat on him without holding your hand with the spatula but rather let them drip down, for this type of treatment moistens the brain moderately.
Then place a woolen cloth soaked in fat or chicken lard on him.
The Twelfth Chapter.
In the treatment of water that has flowed into the eye.
If you become aware of the beginning of water having flowed into the eye, by means of the signs mentioned in the classification, begin to cleanse his head and protect him from all moisture, and bathe him in the bathhouse for several days.
Then shave his head and administer a remedy in the middle of the head, then administer two remedies on the temples if the water began to flow into both eyes or into one eye.
Then cut with the spatula all the veins and sinews under the skin, so that the remedies are in length on the width of the temples, and be careful to prevent bleeding.
If you see anything of it, cut it out from its place with any treatment possible to you, and we will come up with the wisdom in cutting the veins and arteries and preventing hemorrhage.
And there is a tumor located in the thigh under the bones like two ulcers.
Chapter Thirteen.
In cases of chronic eye discharge.
If the eye discharge is chronic and permanent, coming from the arteries and veins in front of the head from outside the skull, and you have confirmed that it is due to an excessive cold humidity which has caused a tumor, then apply the treatment I mentioned earlier for the tumour with which the water flowed down. A tumor in the middle of the head and two on the temples and two under the bones of the thigh, and if you need more apply a tumour to each side of the eye socket with a small mallet.
Chapter Fourteen.
In cases of nasal polyp.
If you treated it as mentioned in the division and the treatment was not successful, then take three olives and crush them and apply the central tumor with a olive oil mortar. Then apply with the mortar of saponaria two tumours above the eyebrows, a little below the hair, and prevent the blood vessel, do not cut it, and this is an image of the saponaria.
Chapter Fifteen.
In cases of a relaxed eyelid tumour.
If the eyelid has relaxed due to disease or moisture, apply one tumor to the eyelid with this crescent-shaped mortar.
And if you wish, apply above the eyebrows a little, two tumours in each side, and separate from the temples, and let each tumour be as long as the eyebrow.
And do not overdo your hand with the mortar, but apply to the extent that one-third of the skin is scorched, and this is the shape of the mortar.
Chapter Sixteen.
For the eyelid.
If her eyelashes have turned inside and obstructed the eye, then there are two kinds of this condition. Either by fire treatment or by the burning medicine, as for treating her with fire then the surgeon should first make him remove his eyelashes if he has any that are curled up so that they become long and even.
So when her eyelashes grow back, bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they have grown and become steady. When they have grown and steadied then make the surgeon sit on a rock, then draw on the eyelid with lamp black a mark in the shape of an ash leaf.
And the mark will start close to the eyelashes then place a cotton swab that has been soaked in white egg or in the spittle of a goat under the eyelid, then protect this shape of its form.
Then knead on the shape that you marked a little at a time, many times until the surface of the skin which is in the shape of an ash leaf burns completely and is visible with its special form, and a sign of the good performance of your work will be when you see the eyelid has formed an eyebrow and the hair has risen from the lash line.
Then lift your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then put on him a cotton swab with fat until the skin crust comes off, then treat him with an ointment until he is cured if God wills. And if anything of the hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then repeat the treatment on that place as you did first, and if the hair is in the lower eyelid then burn it until it returns to its natural position and does not get entangled with the eye lashes. And as for treating him with the burning medicine, it is that you order the surgeon to leave his eyelashes alone so that they become long and even.
Then make from papyrus a picture of the skin, and take from the common soap and from the unextinguished alum each the weight of a dirham or its like, crush them both well together, and do this with a mortar lest it dry. Then spread some on the papyrus you made in the shape of a skin and put it on one eyelid or both, and put a cotton steeped in white egg whites under the eye and the edge of the needle in your stone.
And put your index finger on top of the medication and compress it a little while you move it every time the needle feels the sensation of the medication because it finds a pleasant sensation like fire, so as long as it feels the pleasure leave the medication and move it with your finger, but if the sensation subsides then remove the medication and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has risen as it rises when it is burned by fire or cut, otherwise go over it again with the medication on the place where the medication had not taken effect and did not spread until you achieve your goal and burn the eye, then put cotton soaked in lard on it so that the blister of burns subsides.
Then treat it with the ointment of senna or other until it clears up, and you should be extremely cautious when working so that nothing from the medication falls into the eye, because if the eyelid relaxes after some days I fear that something may fall onto the eye.
Then apply the medication to that part of the eyelid which has relaxed particularly as you did first, then treat it until it clears up, and this is a picture of the skin.
Know that the eyes of people may differ in smallness and largeness, so according to that let your burn be, and it is not a difficult way for those who have an ulcer with this craft.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
For the treatment of corneal ulceration in the eye.
If you have treated the corneal ulcer as we mentioned in the sections on diseases, and your treatment has not been successful, then apply this ointment.
The patient should put his head in your lap and the servant should hold his head firmly between your hands so that it does not move or strike against anything.
Then you put a moistened cotton swab in the white of an egg or in the spittle of a carp on his eyes, and then cover the bandage that has this form.
It is to be made as the shape of an eagle's feather tube from one end which has the ointment and if you wish it is to have a hole in the other end or if you wish it is to be solid like a reed but this type of bandage is better for your work, God willing.
Then you press the corneal ulcer if it is open and remove its discharge or if it is closed then you open it and extract its pus, then put on it the bandage which is very moist so grasp it with your hand until you reach the bone.
And move your hand a little away from the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand does not slip or the patient gets anxious and the bandage falls into the corner of the eye. And if you reached the bone in the first application then do nothing but if not then reapply the bandage again as needed.
And leave it for three days, then put on him a cotton swab with fat and treat him with the dried ointment until he heals. And if forty days pass and he does not heal, then apply to him the hot and sharp medicine until the bone is exposed and refer to what will be mentioned in its section, God willing.
And another way from treating corneal ulcers, which was mentioned by some predecessors: you intentionally cut into the place of the ulcer and then put a thin reed tube in the same cut.
Put into it a quantity of the weight of a dirham of molten lead and hold your hand firmly, without the patient moving at all lest the molten lead flow into his eye. And place on the eye of the patient a wetted lint cloth in white chalk or in water.
For the lead burns the site of the cataract and cures it in a wonderful way, if the cataract is cured with what has been mentioned from the treatment. But if not, then there is no choice but to make an incision into the nose and let the cataract flow back into the course of the nose as will be described in its place specifically.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
Treatment for a cut lip.
A cut in the lip is often called a "cut" and most often occurs in the lips of children. If this cut was treated with what has been mentioned in the division, but treatment did not succeed, then place a small thin iron cautery on it like this.
Its interior is hollowed out to the thickness of a knife blade, then it is placed in the wound with a cauterizer until the treatment reaches the depth of the cut, then it is treated with caustics until it heals, God willing.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
Treatment for cataract that occurs in the mouth.
If a tumour appeared in the root of the gums or in the throat or in the roots of the teeth, then it turned into pus and burst and became a cataract that was treated but did not heal, then you should cauterize with an iron instrument to the size that fits inside the cataract.
Then insert the cauterizer into the cataract while it is red-hot until its tip reaches the depth of the cataract and do this once or twice, then treat it after that with what has been mentioned from treatment until it heals, God willing.
If the material has been cut off and is healthy, then there is no need to uncover the place. Otherwise, it must be uncovered and the dead bone removed as mentioned in its chapter if God wills.
The twentieth part.
For teeth that are loosened or extracted.
If the gums have loosened before due to moisture and the abscesses were treated with medicines but did not heal, then place the head of the instrument on your stone and then put the tube on the molar.
And the cauterizing iron enters into it, held firmly by your hand until the heat reaches the root of the molar. Then lift your hand and return the cauterizing iron as many times as you wish, then fill the abscess with salt water.
And hold it for a moment and then throw him out. For the loosened molar will be set and the gums will become strong and dry the bad moisture.
The twenty-first part.
For a tooth with an abscess.
If the abscess of the tooth is due to cold or it contains a worm and the treatment with medicines did not heal, then apply the caustic on its two faces, either the caustic made of fat or the caustic made by fire.
As for the caustic made of fat, take the fat of a goat and boil it in an iron pot or a shell. Then take a thread and wind it on the end of the instrument, then dip it in the melted fat and place it on the abscessed tooth with the instrument and hold it until it cools down.
Then return it as many times as you wish until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. And if you want to dip a piece of wool or thread in cold fat and place it on the abscessed tooth and put over it the iron instrument protected until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
And as for cauterizing with fire, it is to go towards a copper or iron tube and there be some thickness within the mass so that the heat of the fire does not reach the mouth of the instrument, then take hold of the handle which has its shape and place it on the same part and grasp your hand until the handle cools down do this several times.
If the pain goes away that day itself or on another day, then after that cauterization it is necessary to fill the instrument's mouth with good fat and keep holding it for an hour then throw it. And this is a picture of the handle.
It cauterizes with any end you want and according to what can be done, and this is a picture of the tube.

The Second Chapter Forty-two.
A remedy for a backache.

The Third and Last Chapter.
For the treatment by puncture at the beginning of an abscess.
This affliction often occurs in young children and its first sign is shortness of breath when they move and are active; and you will find at the end of their back a knot that has risen above other knots.

The Fourth and Fortieth Chapter.
For treatment by puncture of gout and joint pains.
If the joint pains are due to cold dampness accumulating in any part of the body, and if the pain occurs in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call that a special gout.
If the gouty person has been treated with the kinds of treatment that we have mentioned in the classification, and his pains have not subsided, then his legs should be wrapped with many folds of linen around the joints, so that the wraps are olive-sized.
And if he needs to apply a poultice to the face of the leg, do it with a compress for plugging. And if the pains have risen to the knees or to other joints, which is often seen, apply the said compress on each knee three or four folds from every side.
And if he needs more than this wrapping, apply a poultice. Do not insert your hand into the wrappings, but rather make it about as thick as the skin only. And if the pains have risen to the hips or to the back, use what we mentioned of the wraps in its place.
And if the pains are only in the hands, apply a poultice around the wrists as two rows turn. And if the pains remain in the fingers, apply a poultice on each joint and on the back of the hand. And if the pains have risen after some days to the elbows or to the shoulders.
Apply poultices to them from every side, and the surgeon should not depart from good management and taking medicines. For if he has improved his diet and evacuated phlegm, then he will recover with this wrapping, God willing.
The Forty-Fifth Chapter.
On the poultice of boils.
If a rupture appears in the abdomen and some of the intestines and gallbladder have descended into the scrotum, and this has begun to be near, it is proper that the surgeon order him to abstain from eating for a day, and to use what laxatives will evacuate his bowels from within.
Then he will lie on his back in front of you, and order him to contract himself until the gallbladder or intestines protrude. Then push it back with your finger. Next, mark a sign resembling half a circle with rounded ends extending up the body under the rupture with a marker.
Then it protects this cautery from rust.
Until it comes out white, the cautery will burn; then pour or throw the cup into its inside and let a servant put his hand on the place so that the cup does not bulge outward. Then he should place a cushion between the patient's legs and another servant tighten him with bandages.
And the last (servant) holds his hands on his chest, then lower the cautery onto the mark itself and hold it firmly upright with the cautery until it reaches the bone or repeat it once more if it does not reach the bone at first.
And preserve your effort from the cup bursting while you are cauterizing lest it gets burnt and in that case, the patient will either die or get a severe injury. And know that if the cautery does not reach the bone, then your work has failed. And let the cautery for children be gentle on their flesh and for adults on theirs.
Then treat the place of cauterization after three days with fat so that the scabbing of fire goes away, then treat it with other ointments until it heals. And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is closed.
And it is necessary that you make his food during the period of treatment soft so that the cup does not bulge out when he uses the toilet. And if he wants to get up after forty days, then use a strong bandage and hold him for another forty days and reduce from fatigue and fullness of food and drink and loud screaming.
For if you treat him with this management like that he will be healed completely, God willing. And I will mention the treatment of rupture by incision in its belly, God willing. As for the rupture which occurs in any part of the abdomen and was initial, then if you want it not to increase, burn the rupture with a round cauterization according to its size. But whatever burns the skin like third-degree burns, then treat it as we have mentioned. It will not increase if God wills; and some of the earlier ones have mentioned that one should apply a splint to the wound in the shape of a triangle.
After learning on the wound with the caustic, making the line that is on the surface at the upper side of the wound and the other line down to the bottom, and then lowering your hand in the middle with a single simultaneous fold; the first fold is easier and better if God wills.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
In the case of a hernia.
If an injury occurs in some organs due to a blow or fall and the pain persists for a long time and medical treatment does not relieve it, then it is advisable that he be wrapped with a splint-shaped pointed instrument; and the fold of each organ should be according to its size, smallness, weakness and strength.
And the pain and swelling subside from it; then he is clear of the first fold. Otherwise, the fold should be applied again to it; because these pains usually transfer from one organ to what is near it, so it should be followed by the fold until the affliction clears up.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
In the case of leprosy.
But the lepers may benefit from the fold with a great benefit, especially the type of leprosy that occurs as a result of the decay of phlegm and blackness.
