Then treat the compress with kneaded bread with honey and all other treatment until he is cured, if God wills.
The 48th Chapter.
In the compress of numbness, when a member is numbed and has been treated with medicines and ointments and bandages but did not recover, then numb the same member by applying compresses according to what it deserves in weight, whether it be heavy or light, let your compress be thick and warm on the skin.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals, and for some numbness that appears on the back of the hand or foot at the exit point of the nerve that moves that member.
And it is not to be undertaken except by someone who knows the structure of the organs and the exit points of the nerves that move the body.
The Forty-Ninth Chapter.
Regarding Leprosy.
If leprosy has reached its final stages and no treatment of the physician's art is effective for him, apply to it a poultice deep enough in relation to the thickness of the skin so that the whiteness disappears and its colour changes.
Then treat it with a precise dose of purslane along with applying rosewater, oryx gum and either red or yellow madder, all in equal parts, mixed together and applied to the affected area until it heals.
The Fifty-First Chapter.
Regarding Cancer Treatment.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you want to stop it, cauterize around it with a circular iron as it turns, and some wise men have said that one should apply a strong poultice on top of it, but I do not see any benefit in this because I fear it will ulcerate, and I have seen that happen several times.
The correct solution is to cauterize around it with a circular iron as we mentioned or with many poultices.
The Fifty-Second Chapter.
Regarding the Treatment of Ulcers.
If an ulcer has occurred on someone and it is delayed in healing, either because of the effective cause of the ulcer or because of the old age of a bloodless person or because of time, and you want to speed up its healing, apply small poultices around it scattered with drops.
Then leave it [alone], for it will hasten its maturation. If you want to dry it completely, then moisten the cauterizing iron whose shape is like this one.
And place it in the middle of the embers until the skin has penetrated. Then let the cauterizing iron be like this below to facilitate the discharge, then treat it as is fitting until it heals.
The Second Chapter Fifty-Two.
For the cauterizing of the appetite.
The eater is a corruption that seeks out the member to consume it, just as fire consumes dry wood. If you see the eater in a place where cauterizing with fire might be beneficial, then heat multiple small and large cauterizing irons in accordance with what is suitable for that location where the eater has appeared.
Then cauterize it from all sides until the corruption is completely eliminated and not a thing remains, then leave it for three days and apply to the cauterized areas powdered sulfur with oil until all the pustules and corruption are evacuated.
Then treat it with medicated ointments for flesh, if you see after three days that the flesh is sprouting a healthy growth without corruption in it; otherwise, redo the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted areas. And the eater may be treated with sharp medicine.
For it has the effect of cauterizing with fire more quickly, and I have mentioned its treatment with sharp medicine in the classification; take that from there whenever you need it.
The Third Chapter Fifty-Three.
For the cauterizing of nails, whether curved or straight.
Often a rough growth occurs in the soles of the feet, which is a harsh thing that troubles the man, and cauterizing it can be done in two ways, either with fire or with hot water.
As for cauterization with fire, it is that you protect the heated instrument resembling a bird's beak made of iron to the extent that it surrounds the pin from all sides and has a thin handle then place it on the pin and turn your hand around the instrument until it reaches the depth of the pin.
And leave it for three days to become suppurated then apply a poultice of crushed wild dough mixed with salt and let the dressing sit on it overnight, so that it detaches from its roots, then treat the wound site with a salve suitable for flesh until it heals, if the splinters are not inverted.
And often it happens on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and legs, so it is necessary to take a tube of copper or iron or bird's beak and place it over the splinter or boil then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube.
And grasp your hand while turning it with a slight flex of the wrist so that the edge of the tube affects the base of the splinter and the hot water finds its way to penetrate into the base of the splinter, and let the patient bear a little the burning of the hot water for an hour.
Then leave it and the splinter will come out with its roots, do this one by one until all that is within the body comes out, then treat the places where they came from after they have come out with ointments suitable for flesh.
The Forty-fourth Chapter.
On cauterization of boils.
If it happens that a boil develops from the chill of a nerve or from quartan fever, or otherwise, then cauterize it four or five times on the spine between each burn and in its chest. And on his stomach cauterize it with an olive oil instrument, then the boil will settle down and speed up the maturation of the cold disease.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
In the case of a boil that occurs in the body.
It may spread in the body with ugly boils that are caused by cold, thick and foul matter. It is advisable at first appearance to burn a thread with a stick of which one end has been lit with fire or the long stalk of thyme or an oblong instrument on each boil.
And the boils may coagulate in their first outbreak on this condition, and that does not increase them and will be eliminated from them the evil effect and they are cured from it except that it is advisable to do that after drawing out the evil with cupping.
Chapter Fifty-Sixth.
In the case of bleeding that occurs when an artery is cut.
Bleeding often occurs from an artery that has been severed when a wound exposes it from outside or when cutting a tumour or case of an organ and the like, making its cutting difficult.
If it happens to someone, then hasten with your hand to the mouth of the artery and put your thumb on it and tighten it gently until the blood is caught under your thumb and nothing comes out from it, then you place a few small and large olives-sized bunches of olive pits in the fire and fumigate them until they are very smoky.
Then you take one of them, either small or large according to the wound and the place where the artery burst, and place it on the same spot after you remove your thumb by the effort and grasp the olive pit until the blood is cut off.
If the bleeding occurs again when you raise your thumb from the mouth of the artery and the olive pit cools down, then take another olive pit by effort from the prepared bunch still in the fire and continue to do that one after another until the blood is cut off.
And preserve, do not burn a stick that will cause another ulcer on the wound, and know that if an artery bleeds from it, then it cannot be cut off, especially if the artery is large, except in one of four ways: either by cauterization as we mentioned earlier, or by cutting it off if it has not been severed. If it has been severed, its ends have contracted and the blood supply has stopped. It may then be stitched with tight stitches or remedies placed on it that can cut off the bleeding and constricting ligatures applied firmly.
And as for anyone who attempts to cut it with a ligature or by constricting with a burn or placing heated objects and the like, in that case, it will not stop bleeding at all, except rarely. If one of those cases occurs without the presence of a doctor or medication, he should immediately place his index finger on the wound itself as we have described.
And he should constrict it very tightly until the blood is blocked and comes out from above the wound, as well as the vessel and finger. And the cold water does not move away from him unless he is frozen, which causes the blood to coagulate and stop. During this time, one looks at what it needs of bandages or medication.
The Second Chapter.
In incisions and cuts, bleeding from wounds and the like.
Khalaf said: We have mentioned in the first chapter all diseases that are cured with the cautery and burnt medication, their cause and reasons, and their tools and forms.
And I follow in this chapter the same approach as it is, so that the student can easily find what he seeks.
It is necessary for you, my sons, to know that this chapter contains some of the most important matters from the first chapter concerning the cautery.
And because of that, a warning is necessary in this chapter, as the work done in it often leads to excessive bleeding with which life goes, when an artery or vein is opened, or a growth, abscess, or surgical wound is cut into, or an arrow or stone is extracted, and similar matters accompanied by great peril and death most often.
And I advise you to beware of falling into what is uncertain for you. For in this craft, there are types of people with various ailments, some of whom may tire of their illness and desire death.
For great is the suffering of one whose affliction is long and who, because of his illness, has come to a decision that indicates death. And there are some who will expend their wealth in your favor, and with it purchase hope for health from their disease; so do not assist those who have this description at all.
Let your caution be stronger than your eagerness and desire, and do not proceed to anything of that sort unless you are certain with a clear knowledge in yourselves of the good outcome. And apply in all the treatment of your patients the precept of knowledge and warning them of what leads to safety.
For in that you have an aid to the acquisition of praise, glory, remembrance and thanks. May Allah guide you, O my sons, and not prevent you from the truth and success; for it is in His hand, there is no God but He.
And I have placed this chapter in sections according to what has come before regarding the treatment of an old person, so that what you seek from it will be clear to you, if God wills.
The First Chapter.
In the treatment of water that accumulates on the heads of children.
For this affliction often occurs in children at birth if the mother has pressed the child's head with too much force, and it may also occur from a hidden cause that is not known.
And I have not seen this affliction in anyone other than children, and all of those whom I have seen among them die quickly from it. That is why I have seen the treatment for it to be neglected. And I saw a child whose head was filled with water and his head swelled every day. Until the child could no longer sit up on his own due to the swelling of his head and the moisture increasing, until he died.
This moisture is either between the skin and bone or beneath the bone on the peritoneum, the operation in this case if the moisture is between the skin and bone and the tumor is small should be cut with a single incision through the middle of the head until the moisture flows and here is the figure of the scalpel.
If the moisture increases and the tumor becomes greater, then make two intersecting incisions in this shape:.
And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and its sign is that you see the stitching of the head opened from every side and the water sinks when you press it with your hand to inside, and not lightly on that, then make three incisions in the middle of the head in this shape.
After the incision the moisture all comes out, then the incisions are tightened with thread and cloth, then it is covered from above with a poultice and oil until the fifth day, then the dressing is removed and the wound is treated with fat and ointments, and do not leave the head tightly fastened and feed the child with dry food that has little moisture.
until the part becomes strong and is healed, another prescription for the incision is to look where the bone of the tumor appears and where the water gathers because it may be at the back of the head or at the front or on the right or on the left.
You are meant by the incision where the tumor appears and the water fills, then make an incision as much as you can and be careful not to cut a vein so that there is bleeding and the child dies from that bleeding along with the evacuation of the moisture.
The Second Chapter.
Cutting the two veins behind the ears known as the Husaysin.
Whenever a sudden illness is presented to the eyes or to the chest and that was timed but did not recover with medication, then told the treatment in that cutting these two veins.
If you wanted to cut both of them, you should shave the head of the abscess with a razor then rub the place with a coarse cloth so that the artery becomes visible. Then tie the neck of the abscess with its thread and look where the sweat is oozing out and the places hidden behind the ears, because they are usually not hidden except in some people.
Then learn on them with ink and then cut them off with a sharp knife in cuts up to the bone, all over the head. If you wanted, insert the knife under the artery and push it upwards by cuts and the length of the cuts will be about two fingers bound together.
If the sweat duct was cut, blood would come out in a pulsating flow to the front and bandage. If the artery did not become visible to touch, you should calculate from the ear after counting three fingers then learn with ink and incise up to the bone, which should.
The blood will clot into a pad of six or seven pieces in the bandage, and perhaps more or less all that according to what you see from the strength of the abscess and the filling of its arteries. Then look at the wound, if something remains from the membrane on the bone, cut it off.
So that a hot ulcer is not exposed, then bandage the wound with a thread from coarse linen and treat it with ointments until it heals.
The Third Chapter.
Cut out the arteries in the groin.
If a man has a chronic abscess or acute inflammation from hot fluids and heat in the groin muscles or severe prolonged headache and similar things and he was treated with various types of medical treatment, but that did not cure him, then we have tried to cut out the arteries from the groin or burn them as we have described.
The object of action in this case is to shave the hair on the forehead, where a vein lies exposed. This vein becomes apparent from its pulse and it is hardly concealed, except in some individuals.
Or if it is very cold and has become less apparent to you, then have him tie a cloth over his neck so that the vein becomes more visible. Then you should compress the area with a cloth or apply warm water until the vein appears clearly and distinctly. Then take hold of the surgical instrument which is shown here. Then you will carefully remove the skin with it until you reach the vein, then insert a hook into it and pull it upwards until you bring it out of the skin and free it from the membranes that are under it on all sides. If the vein is narrow, shape it with the end of the hook. Then cut from it a portion as the ends of which diverge, and pinch. Do not cause bleeding because if it does not become severed or cut off then the blood will not flow at all. Then remove blood from six to three aquae-spissae.
If the vein is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread. The thread may either be of silk or from the tendons of a bowstring so that before the wound closes decay does not occur and bleeding results.
Then cut the part between the ligatures. You should do this at that time or later, and if you wish to compress it tightly against the bone with a flat spatula until its ends become severed then it will take the place of this action by itself or better as we said.
But if the vein has a fever or is in an unbalanced condition, because compression can help to eliminate moisture and it becomes more useful. After having separated the veins, the place should be packed with the poultice made from plantain leaves and a compress placed on top of it. And after the swelling subsides, he will treat with dry remedies that nourish flesh and with poultices until he heals, if God wills.
If bleeding occurs from an artery during your operation, hasten to cut it off with a knife or fill the area with alum and tighten your hand until the blood stops. If you do not have something for this, place your finger on the area until the blood clots.
And if you want to compress the area with cold water until the swelling subsides and bind it as is proper, and what is lighter and easier than cutting the artery is to crush it with this tweezers-like forceps after having secured the two ends with thread.
And lower it very tightly until it reaches the bone and the artery is cut in two places so that what is between its ends becomes separate, for it will not stick with this forceps at all. And this is a picture of the tweezers.
The tweezers with sharp blades are similar to the two small scimitars except that they are much duller than the knife, for if they were as sharp as the knife, cold would reach them more quickly and the flesh would not stop bleeding promptly. If they have some coarseness in them then hot embers will stick to them.
And you have cut the flesh promptly, and this work is better than all works and lighter and easier; let there be space between the blades equal to the thickness of a finger.
The Fourth Chapter.
In treating the continuous flowing of hot tears into the eyes.
If the tears are continuous and their flowing is from the blood vessels on the head from outside and there is no benefit in treating them with any medical treatment or medicine, and you see that the face of the sick person has become red. And he feels in his forehead a pimple like the buzzing of ants and his eyes are drooping, wet and their lashes have become swollen and their eyelids have become sunken from the intensity of the tears. And so the earlier physicians were compelled to resort to this operation which they call the treatment with a sword, that is for the patient to shave the hair on his forehead.
Then make three incisions on the forehead in a straight line along its length. The length of each incision is about two fingers' breadth. One is parallel to the length of the nose at the centre of the forehead, the second a little away from the movement of the muscles on the temple, and the third from the opposite side.
And you keep yourself from cutting the arteries which are on either side, and move your hand away from the connection of the cheekbones. And after each incision make a space of three folded fingers, and with you be sponges made of cloth or many soft pieces of linen so that blood may be drained.
Then insert the sharp instrument into both sides as shown in these drawings. Then insert it from the incision next to the temple up to the middle one, and scrape away all the skin in between the two incisions along with the serous membrane on the bone. Then do the same from the middle incision up to the third one, then take out this instrument. And then insert into the first incision another instrument called "skinnia" sharp on one side and blunt on the other, as shown in this drawing.
And its sharp side is turned upwards towards the flesh covered with skin, and its blunt side is towards the bone. Then push it until it reaches the middle incision and cut all the vessels that come from the head to the eyes without reaching the outer skin.
Then do the same from the middle incision to the other one. And when a moderate amount of blood has flowed, squeeze out the clots of coagulated blood from each wound. Then make a thread of cloth and put it into each incision, placing on it a poultice that has been mixed with wine, oil or vinegar and fat.
So that a hot abscess does not form. And on the third day, the dressing will be removed and a lot of lukewarm water will be used to cleanse it, then it will be treated with a plaster made from saffron mixed with rose ointment and all what is used for treating wounds until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Five.
Treatment of discharge and fluxes from the eyes into the head.
Whenever a person has frequent and severe discharges from the head, and their eyelashes are weak and hanging, and their conjunctiva is inflamed with shedding of lashes. And there is a severe and painful headache, followed by persistent coughing, so know from these symptoms that the discharge comes from many deep veins. The best treatment for this is to have the doctor put his finger into the patient's forehead, then make a single incision in the middle of the forehead.
And there is a severe and painful headache, followed by persistent coughing, so know from these symptoms that the discharge comes from many deep veins. The best treatment for this is to have the doctor put his finger into the patient's forehead, then make a single incision in the middle of the forehead. Or elevate it slightly with the probe and begin the incision from the left eyebrow to the right, the incision being to the bone, and keep your hand away from the moving muscles of the jaw as you make the cut, until the bone is exposed and all blood is cleaned with a sponge.
Then separate the cut lips of the incision with cotton or a piece of linen, and tighten from above with thread and soak the thread in drink and oil so that a hot abscess does not form. And when you have finished treating it and see that the hot abscess has been cured, then scrape the bone until fresh flesh begins to grow.
Then treat it with the dried remedy that promotes flesh growth, such as taking equal parts of barley flour and four parts of calamine, mixing them to make a paste, and using it to promote flesh growth in similar wounds.
Chapter Six.
Treatment of what is discharged into the ear.
All that is discharged into the ear falls into one of four types: either a metallic stone, such as iron or glass, or a plant seed, like almonds and kernels, or something liquid, like water and vinegar.
If an animal, then when a stone falls into the ear or a type of stone which does not exceed in the ear, receive the sun in the ear. Then if you see the stone, smear some linseed oil or senna on it and try to remove it by head movement or by irrigating with kandus. Close the nostrils when the hiccup arrives after you put a cord of wool or hair around the ear and stretch the ear upwards, many times it comes out with this treatment. If it does not come out then try to remove it by the soft sponge shown here.
If it comes out by the sponge and does not then try to remove it by a soft, lightly curved blind forceps. If it does not come out with that, then make a tube of copper and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal.
Close what is around the tube with a thick paste of gum and oil so that the air does not find a way out except by the tube. Then pull it with your breath, pulling strongly and often it comes out with this. If it does not come out as we described then take some attar of the Nabataeans or some well-cut resin which birds are taken with a little and put it in the end of the syringe.
After wrapping it tightly with a strong thread then insert it into the ear canal gently after the ear has dried of moisture. If it does not come out with all that we described, then proceed to the incision before the hot abscess or swelling occurs.
The recipe for the incision is that you shave the hair around the ear first and let out to him from the blood as much as his strength allows. Then sit the patient before you and turn their ear upwards and make a small cut in the upper part of the ear where the cartilage meets the skin, in its lowest place.
And the incision will be crescent-shaped until it reaches the stone then remove it with as much of the instruments as you can, then sew up the incision quickly and treat it until it heals.
As for the thing that has fallen into the ear from one of the grains that grow and swell, try to remove it as mentioned earlier. If this does not work, take a thin and fine probe in this shape.
Try to cut that type of grain which has fallen into the ear with it, and you do this if you are certain that that grain has become moistened by the steam of the ear until it becomes small pieces. Then take them out with a blunt instrument or a fine forceps or with a blunt spatula.
As we have mentioned, it is easy to remove it. But as for the water that has entered the ear, you should use a syringe with a cotton swab first, and fill his ear with something of dry flax, while he is lying on that ear which has the water in it. Then if it comes out by this.
But if it does not come out, take a lot of pebbles that are smooth on the length of the fingers and heat them slightly with fire. The patient should then have one of those pebbles inserted into his ear canal, and lie down on one foot from this side, and strike another stone against the stone that is in the ear.
Then he continues to do this with a pebble, stone by stone, until all the water comes out. The water may also come out if one takes from wool or flax, one strand, and puts its tip into the ear, while warming up the other end in the fire until it catches on fire. Then take another strand of wool.
He continues to do that until all the water comes out or pulls it with a syringe, as mentioned earlier in the pebble. But if an animal has entered and is small in size, like a mouse and so forth, then handle it as I have mentioned in the section.
If its body is large and visible to the touch, try to remove it with forceps and a spatula, and this is easier than all that gets stuck in the ear. And if there is a worm generated in the ear, which you have treated with what I mentioned in the section on the worms, but your treatment did not succeed.
It is necessary to look at the ear in the sun; if something of the lice appears, then take it out with a spatula or fine forceps. If nothing appears, take a hollow tube resembling this image.
Narrow at the bottom and wide at the top, insert the thin end into the ear as far as it can be pushed in. Then squeeze with a strong pressure until all the lice come out. If they do not exit, plug around the tube with wax as I mentioned to you about the stone.
If they do not come out as we have mentioned, use the quatrants which I have mentioned and the pioneers have tried in killing the lice. You will find that in the treatise on quatrants. Pouring ointments and medications into the ear with this device. And here is its form:
As you see, it is made from copper or iron, narrow at the bottom and a small hole in it, wide at the top. If you want the chamber inside the tube to be of strong iron, if you want, take a rod and wrap tightly with cotton wrapped tightly on its end.
Then pour the oil or juice or whatever medicine you want into the tube and it is in the ear. Then insert the rod with the cotton on top, and press with your hand pressing moderately until the oil penetrates deep into the ear canal and you feel it.
So that the oil is inside the ear canal, and let what you pour into the ear have been warmed slightly in the fire. And beware lest the thing which forms a blister inside be very cold or very hot; for the ear does not tolerate that.
The Seventh Chapter.
In the treatment of the obstructing mass in the ear.
Some children may come out from their mothers' wombs and ears unperforated.
And also some people may have a mass in the ear canal from an injury or a growth there, and this mass may be deep within the ear hole that is not visible to the eye.
And it may protrude a little outside the incision and be visible to sight, so that what protrudes into the depth of the ear and is not visible to sight usually indicates difficulty in recovery. And that which becomes visible to sight should have the patient's ear placed in the sun. And look at it; if you see the membrane exposed, open it with a fine needle and this is its appearance:
Its end will be exposed a little, limited in some of it, and the rest of the needle smooth on both sides so as not to harm the ear. If the membrane has grown into fat in the ear canal, grasp it with a fine forceps and cut it off gently until all the fat is removed.
If the membrane is deep in the ear, take a fine metal file that is smooth and heat it slightly then insert it into the ear canal. If you feel the membrane with what the patient experiences as heaviness of hearing, smooth it off gently.
And be careful not to cut the ear canal's ligament, then put a thread into the ear as big as the size of the incision that was stuck in the Egyptian ointment. Do this for some days until you are sure that the wound is healed or take a thread and dip it in water and sprinkle on it zanj a powder.
And use it, if you see the ear has become inflamed, apply a hot poultice. Then remove the thread and replace it with another thread that was stuck in the quinine made from rose oil so that the inflammation subsides, then treat it until it heals.
If bleeding occurs, dip a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and apply all the treatment that stops the mentioned bleeding as is written in the chapter of the cautery.
The Eighth Chapter.
In the treatment of ulcers which protrude in the ear canal.
These growths which appear on the eyelids can be moist or dry. One should grasp them with a forceps or a pincer and cut them off at their roots with a lancet, then apply powdered alum to the place.
If there is bleeding from it, plug it with a soft lentil-shaped pessary. It is better than the previous method and often returns if something remains of its roots. If cooked over fire, those roots are burned off and it does not return.
The ninth chapter.
In the treatment of the conjunctival redness.
A thing resembling redness in its tightness and thinness often appears in the conjunctiva.
And therefore it is called redness, which is the gathering of a thick moisture in the upper and lower eyelid. The treatment for it is to look; if the redness protrudes towards the surface of the eyelid, move it in all directions. Then make an incision on its edge.
Then gently scrape it from all sides until it is gone, then grasp it with a pincer and cut it off. If you cannot cut it without cutting the eyelid itself, do not worry about the growth; if the incision is large, sew it up and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, do not worry about it; the ointment will cure it and heal it. And if the redness inclines towards the inner surface of the eyelid towards the front, flip the eyelid over and grasp the redness with a pincer without cutting an incision, then scrape it from all sides.
And if the eyelid has been cut, it will not be harmed. Then wash the eye with salty water after cutting off the redness and treat the area with what cures until the growth is healed.
The Tenth Chapter.
In the treatment of cataract which appears in the eye lid.
Cataract is a lump which forms in the upper layer of the eyelid, and it most often affects children, weighing down their eyes and exposing them to sandstorms, preventing them from looking at the light of the sun. So that tears may run quickly to them.
Therefore you see them constantly leaning on their faces and sleeping with it, and their eyelids are moist beneath the eyebrows, where there is inflation and swelling of the cataract. If you press your fingers to the place, you will feel the cataract between the two lids. And the treatment involves the operator placing his head in front of them.
Then take a linen cloth and prepare an end from it, and make a circle with the end of that thread to cover the cataract completely. Then place it on him and press with your fingers all around to gather the cataract in the middle of the circle.
Then make a cut in the middle of that moisture with a razor, making a slit that is not wider than the incision and is as deep as it should be. As for depth, it is necessary to cut through all the skin until reaching the cataract.
In most cases, the cataract will protrude from the cut in the form of a white fatty piece. You should draw it out with a cloth that you have wrapped between your fingers outside, while rotating your hand left and right until it is freed. And beware not to increase the incision so that the razor does not touch the eye and harm it.
If the cataract does not protrude from the first incision, it is necessary to increase the incision a little gently until it appears, then draw it out as we mentioned. Then dip a cloth in vinegar and water and place it on the place and bandage it with a compress. And some people crush salt on it.
Place it in the cavity of the incision so that what remains of that moisture may dissolve. Then treat it until he heals, and if there occurs in the place a hot tumour cure him with poultices made soft until he heals.
The Eleventh Chapter.
On Kinds of Eye Bandages.
If there sprouts on the eyelid an abnormal growth below the natural lashes and you shave it, then it will harm the eye and cause a variety of diseases such as perpetual tears, slackness of the lid, white spots and thickening until that becomes a reason for blindness.
The eye is bandaged in four ways either with a caustic by fire or with a sharp medicine as mentioned earlier in the chapter on cauterization or it is bandaged with patches and stitches or with papyrus as I have remembered.
You should make the head of the needle in your fist, then turn the eyelid with your left hand. If it turns over, else insert a thread into it from below the lid and pierce the needle with the thread from above, that being near to the hair itself, and pull the thread up by the lid.
Turn it back with the thumb, then cut in the inner eyelid without the excess hair with a sharp instrument from the larger notch to the smaller one, then let the thread pass and put under the lid a small pad of cotton or cloth, then stitch over the lid with stitches.
Like the shape of a mulberry leaf, except that it is necessary for the shape to be as much raised on the lid as you want because people differ in this and some need that part of the eyelid cut off according to how slack the lid is.
And some need less cut, all that according to how slack the lid is. Then stitch with a needle along the lines you sewed and start from the larger notch to the smaller one, and the single incision will be near the natural hair as thick as the thumb.
Then, the forceps are introduced into one of the corners of the skin and it is peeled off completely. The lips are then gathered with a thread of fine woolen yarn and the blood is wiped away and what remains of the threads is pressed onto the eyebrows with something adhesive.
If you want to do that and otherwise don't care, then the stitching and threads remain for about three or four days then it is treated. If you want, leave the wound without stitching and treat what dries up and constricts; indeed the eyelid rises with closing the wound and its stitching is better.
This is one of the faces from the shaving that the ancients mentioned except that it includes hardship on the eyelid and it is a good job with no danger in it. And another face in the shaving also is that you shape on the eyelid a form like the shape of an Aspen leaf as we have described. Then the eyelid is raised with three tweezers which are separate or joined in this shape:.
Then what remains of the eyelid is cut off with a small scissors in this shape: cut gently.
If you cannot hold the tweezers and your hands are not steady, take a thread with a needle and insert it in the middle of the shape, and another thread near the larger fold and another thread near the smaller fold, then gather the threads gently between your fingers and lift them gently with your hand.
Then raise the peeled skin as we have described and gather the edges of the wound with stitching and treat it until it heals. If a red and warm spot appears when you cut or incise, calm that swelling with calamine lotion and similar soothing ointments.
And the lower eyelid may also turn its lashes, it is necessary to use what we have mentioned from cutting and stitching and shaving with fire and from the strong remedy and shaving with fire or from the strong remedy more clear and lighter on the eyelid than cutting and stitching.
The cleansing with reeds is of this form, that you turn the eyelid and make a cut from inside as I have described, then you make two or four thin slits in length on the eyelid and their width less than the width of the incision.
And I have applied them on the edges of both sides where the threads stick to them then I have joined it gently on what remained from the eyelid and pulled tight the slits from both sides tightly, and left it for some days because the tightened skin dies and turns black and rotten.
Until it falls on its own, if I delayed then I have removed them with the curler and treated until it heals. If the swelling increased the eyelid lifted and the eyelashes of the eye did not droop, and this is the form of the slits made in this manner and this length in the width as well:
The Twelfth Chapter.
On lifting the annoying hair from the eye with a needle.
If there was a hair or two to be dealt with, that one takes a thin needle and inserts into it a thread of fine silk smoothed out then gathers its ends and ties them in a gentle knot, the length of the thread being about an arm's length.
Then thread on the needle another thin thread after it, smoothed out in the knot and tied its ends if you wish then the surgeon puts his head close to yours near the sun so that he may see what he is doing because it is delicate work then one inserts the needle with the thread into the root of the excessive hair.
And executes it in the eyelid with a wheel until it comes out from above the natural hair then pulls the thread up to above the knot and inserts into that knot the excessive hair if it was one or two or three no more.
Then you pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the thread in the eyelid along with the natural hair. If you pulled the thread and the hair did not come out with it, then pull the thread down by the thread which you had threaded into it until the thread comes out from the upper hole.
Then insert the hair into it and pull them in such a way that they rise up to the upper hole, until you see them with your eyes. Then release the ligatures and thread and bring out [the threads] and tighten the eye and leave it tightened for two or three days until the hair takes its place and flesh grows on it.
If the hair is short, then either add to it a long hair from natural hair so that they rise together; or else leave it until it grows after some time, and when it does, raise it.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of a knot that occurs in the upper eyelid of the eye.
The one to which this knot occurs is called a nodule and it will be either natural or acquired. The acquired one will be from the remnants of an incision, cut, or scratch and so on.
And the procedure in it is to incise that remnant and separate its edges, then make a thread of linen between them and tie it until it heals. And it should not be treated with things that dry up and constrict.
If you do that, the knot will return worse than it was. So use in it things that soften such as the lye, oil of linseed with a small amount of quicklime, and a paste made from castor oil mixed with something of varnish and applied to the thread.
And the way to treat it is to try with all means that it should not adhere again in its original form, and this procedure which we mentioned earlier was only a treatment for the knot, not so that the shape of the place returns exactly as it was at first.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of a knot that occurs in the lower eyelid.
This tight constriction, which is from the skin itself, is called the real stricture. It is natural and it occurs because of a wound or cut or incision or something similar.
The method of procedure for it is that you take a needle with twine and insert it in the flesh and lead it from the left flank to the right one until the string becomes at both ends of the flesh, then you stretch the flesh upwards by the needle and cut it off with a broad razor.
If the shape of the eyelid returns to what is correct, and if not then you take a spatula and place it on the place of the incision and turn with it the eyelid and make two cuts inside the fold of the eyelid and their ends will meet so that there will be a corner. Until they meet, its shape will become similar to this shape.
And then you remove that flesh as much as the sharp edge of it is below what follows the eyelid, and then gather the scattered parts with two stitches to sew him with a woolen thread, and then treat him with the mentioned soothing and ointments until he heals.
And if the constriction was caused by a cut or suture or incision, then it is necessary to make a small cut besides the eyelashes as mentioned before, then spread between the lips with ointment as we have mentioned.
In short, the treatment of the constriction, whether from above or from below, is to perform an operation according to what presents itself regarding the appearance of the constriction, for it may be many different forms, and the master craftsman finds a way with whatever means he can.
Until its shape returns to its natural form or approaches it, and the same disease directs you to what is suitable for him in terms of work and tool in most cases.
Chapter Fifteenth.
In the case of the eyelid being sewn up to the eyebrow or the caruncle.
It may be presented to many people that the upper eyelid is sewn up with the white of the eye, preventing it from moving easily and obstructing its natural functions, so you must insert the tip of your forceps under the eyelid.
You raise it up or stretch it with a tweezers then cut the adhesion with a soft forceps which is not cutting sharply like that of a surgical scalpel so as not to agitate the patient, and your cut will be as if you were peeling off that adhesion.
And wait until the eyelid returns to its natural state and all adhesion is gone, then pour into the eye a salty water that washes it with or inject into it from a vial of Zarangi solution dissolved in water, then spread between the eyelid and the eye with a cotton strip.
And place above the eye a wool moistened with egg white, and after three days use the syringes filled until it clears.
Chapter Sixteenth.
In cutting the horn of the nails and cutting the membranes of the tendons.
The horn of the nail is either in two kinds, either it is brittle and resembles a hard thin cord, or it is not brittle and resembles frozen moisture white if touched with iron or if you take hold of it with tweezers it is cut.
But it didn't stick with the tweezers, and both kinds start from the larger tendon until it spreads a little, little until it covers the view and prevents light and eye movement, and the face of work in cutting it that the operator puts his head in your hand.
Then he opens his eyes and lifts the eyelid with your hand, then you take hold of the horn with a tweezers that has little bend and extend it upwards, then take a needle and enter into it a hair from horse or cow hair and a strong thread, and bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it in the middle of the horn.
Perform it with a needle and tie it with a thin thread, then extend it upwards. Remove the layer of skin on the side of the nail that follows the cuticle as if you were spreading it by a hair until the end, then cut the rest at the base of the nail with a gentle lancet or small scissors, leaving its natural nail flesh.
So that the blood does not constantly ooze from what is cut. The nail plate can be extended with a drill alone or with thread as we said, then remove the end with a smooth lancet as shown in this picture:.
And take care that the lancet does not touch the corneal epithelium, so a cleft forms in it and the cuticle is affected. Then after cutting, put some powdered salt or rhubarb powder into the eye and leave it until another day then treat it as needed until it heals.
If the nail is not sensitive and you were unable to insert a needle or fix it with a drill, this type of nail is often treated with medication so that it heals as I described in the classification. And if you want to cut it, open the patient's eye.
Take a gentle lancet with a soft and smooth edge as shown in this picture:. Remove the nail with it from above gently. If you see that it is crumbling and disintegrating, apply the extract only to this part of your eye with rhubarb powder or red camphor powder or powdered salt and close your eye for another day.
Then redo the procedure on it until all of it is gone, unless a hot abscess forms in your eye; leave them and treat the hot abscess until it heals then redo the procedure on it with the drill until it heals. And as for the flesh of the nail bed.
If the nodule causes severe pain to the eye, tie it with a drill and cut off some of it without being meticulous in the cutting so that bleeding does not occur then apply red camphor or rhubarb powder to the wounds until it heals.
Chapter Seventeen.
In cutting the cataract and whatever grows from excess flesh in the eye.
There may grow in the eyes of some people red fleshed tissue that becomes intertwined, until it covers what is seen or approaches or overflows onto the conjunctiva and perhaps the conjunctiva turns outside and resembles a pomegranate flower.
And the procedure is that the surgeon places his head close to the patient, then opens the patient's eyes and catches all of this red flesh with appropriate forceps.
Or he catches it with a hook or stylet then cuts out the first bit, one by one, until all of it is cut away and preserved from the eye lest it harm it during the operation; and your cutting for him should be either with the razor which we described in cutting the cataract, or a small pair of scissors. As is done to take hold of threads as illustrated in the chapter at the end of this book.
If you have cut it and all the cataract has been removed, fill the eye with ground salt or sprinkle in a red powder like some of the potent medicines, and place on the eye from outside white lint to prevent the warm swelling.
If there remains something of the cataract and blood overflows on you and you fear the warm swelling, leave the eye alone and treat it with what will calm the swelling then return to it and operate until it is cured; do likewise for the excess flesh that appears in the eye from this type.
Unless it is fitting for you to avoid treating any weak eye by the method of nature or exposure with ironwork, and not to put your hand into anything from these works until you see that that organ is capable of that work.
Chapter Eighteen.
In cutting the threads from the eye.
The ways of red veins are to become entwined on the eye, in whoever is prevented from seeing; and it weakens the eye with the passage of time. You should first look at the eye in which the red veins exist; if its eye is strong and there is no other disease except the red veins.
So when that, then you order the patient to place his head in your lap; then tie those veins with a single or double needle according to what is proper for you. And make the needles soft in their bend like this:.
or be two joined needles in one body like this:.
Then you catch with a soft scissor those veins gently and clean the blood from time to time until you see the eye, for that red vein has gone from it and the bleeding has stopped. And be careful not to harm the eye with the tips of the scissors; do this work at noon in front of the sun.
And be very careful in your work so that you do not cut anything other than those veins. Then, when you are finished, prick the eye with a green or red needle to eat up what is left of the blood vessels. And if you cannot take it all out at that time, press the eye with something to calm the pain of the eye.
And leave it for some days until the pain subsides and the hot swelling calms down; then return to work on it like this with exactly the same eye until this picture of the scissor is free from its scar.
And leave it and the patient's head will be in the lap of the apprentice, while the other wipes away the tears and clears the anterior and posterior part of the eye, and [the student] holds the original in the work to open the eye with openings like triangles or squares.
He kneads and the patient's head will be in the lap of the apprentice, while the other wipes away the tears and clears the anterior and posterior part of the eye, with the choice to start cutting from the top of the eye or from its bottom. The first is that two needles are sewn up in the upper eyelid, one at the end of it and the other at its beginning.
Take it between the middle fingers and thumbs then attach strings from underneath them, then take it between the index finger and thumb and gently withdraw your hand until all the skin appears. Cut the western smaller one if you cut with scissors or if you cut with a light forceps.
The covered part will be sewn on the artery and all the skin will dry out until it rises above the swelling, do not cut the tension as the sweat and blood will become sticky on you.
Then cut with the scissors everything above and below the ligature so that there is no remaining flap except in the crevice. If you can lift it from the crevice, scrape with a razor as it is better and may heal in some people.
And if you cut it, the bleeding would stop after a few days, he would be at ease and in peace from the hot swelling then redo the work on him.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
In returning the feather to the nose.
The physicians call the feather Nasoura, if it was treated with strong medicine or the sharp drug as mentioned above and did not heal, there is no cure for it except to cut into the swelling at its maturity and to extract all the moisture or pus that is in it.
Until the bone is exposed, if the bone has been exposed and you saw in it putrefaction or discoloration then remove it with this instrument.
And it is called the roughness of the head which is made from Indian iron, and its head is bent like a file that has been engraved with a fine carving, then you put it on the place of decay from the bone, then turn it between your fingers as you moisten your hand a little until you know that the decay has been removed.
You do that several times then treat the place with the dried adherent medicines, if you have closed the place and new flesh has grown in it and the bleeding has stopped and there were forty days without suppuration or swelling or any accident occurring in it.
Know that he is healed, otherwise there is no trick but to return the trephine to the nasal opening in this manner and it is that you uncover the bone again with a heated iron or sharp drug. If the bone has been uncovered, take a glowing ember in the form of:.
The tip of the iron is triangular and its handle cone-shaped, bent towards the point as you see. Then put it on the bone itself near the vertex and slightly farther from the eye, then turn your hand with the ember until the bone is perforated and the sound is perceived.
That the breath comes out of him if he holds his hand on his nose. Then press the place with adhesive, dried drugs as I have taught you. If the flesh has grown back and the place is hard, then the material which was directed to the outside returns to the nostril, and that will be easier for the patient, God willing.
Chapter Twenty.
Reopening a perforated eye socket.
If the eye socket has been perforated and no affliction or defect has occurred in the sight, then the trephine should be removed and it is cleaned in the quiver, then a thin felt pad is placed in the orbit without any constraint and moistened with a fine dressing.
Then a poultice made from vinegar, myrrh, galbanum and aloes is placed on the eye. Then the eyelid is pulled upwards over the dressing for many benefits. The recipe for the bandage is to take several linen cloths and fold each one into four folds making them into many.
Then they are placed one on top of another as much as the eye needs, then it is pulled over with a strong linen cloth and the felt pad is replaced with dressing again without constraint. Then the felt pad is removed and the eye is left closed for a day and night.
If the bandage relaxes in between, it should be pulled tight again. Then remove the bandage after a day and night as we said. If you see that the eye has returned to its place and if not, then repeat the dressing, poultice, tightening and placing of the pad until it returns.
Chapter Twenty-One.
Concerning the amputation of limbs.
If a hernia appears in the skin of the limb and swells and protrudes outside the integument like a swelling and its shape is distorted from that of man, because one wishes to cut it, then do as I have described.
And that is to enter a needle from below upwards into the root of the swelling, and then another needle in it with a doubled thread from the direction of the groin, and proceed with it while leaving the first needle as it was.
Then cut the place of the doubled thread and tie it with some of the swelling around the needle and bind it tightly, then take out the needles and put on the eye a wool moistened in egg white and let it stay until the threads drop off along with the swelling, then treat the eye as is strengthening to it.
Until the wound heals, and it may be to tighten the swelling from all sides with a bandage in a circle until the eye becomes swollen even more tightly then it will be irrigated with a fine syringe reaching into the depth of the eye and letting out the watery fluid and lowering the eye and calming down on its place then tightening it until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
Concerning the treatment of cataracts.
This disease which is called cataract, indeed it is a drop gathering in the eye like falling water but it does not contain it, and the work done in that is to have the operator sit on an upright chair then take his head with your hands from both sides.
And move it until you see the drop going down with your eye, then steady it and do not let it go and the light will pass and the operator will see things as he used to see them, and if it does not go down below as we mentioned, know that it is water, and if it does not prepare for the drop to go down as mentioned.
If not, then sit the patient in front of you and take a thin probe and pass it above the membranous tendon slightly at the point of connection between the ligament and the membranous tendon in the angle until the material comes out.
If it comes out, drop into the eye warm water which may be mixed with myrrh or water that has been boiled with rue and then treat with the rest of the treatment until he recovers.
Chapter Twenty-Three.
We have mentioned the kinds of water in the section and which is suitable for the cup, with a detailed explanation so that you take it from there on good health. So when this happens, then sit the patient in front of you elevated towards the light near the sun.
And bind the good eye with a bandage and tie it tightly, then lift the eyelid of the eye with your left hand if the eye which has water is the left one or with your right hand if the eye is on the right.
Then place the tip of the cup near the angle with a firm finger in the same white part of the eye from the side of the smaller angle, then push the cup with force while turning it with your hand until it penetrates into the whiteness of the eye and you feel that the cup has reached something empty.
And it should be that the distance of the cup going into depth is equal to the distance from the white part to the black part, which is the angle of the eye. For the copper [part] can be seen by the observer seeing the eye because of the clarity of the membranous tendon, then the cup goes up to the place where there is water.
Then grasp it downwards, once after another, if the water flows out from its cup then the patient sees what his eye has opened up to him from its cup and the cup in his eye, then he settles a little. If the water rises then lower it again without the cup coming out.
If it settles and does not rise, then take out the instrument gently while holding its tip a little at a time until it dissolves in water some of pure white Anadranis salt. Then wash the eye from within with it, and afterwards place on the whole eye some soft wool or flax that has been soaked in it.
With a piece of red and white fat, and tying it with the good eye. And as for us and people in our time, we put on it crushed camomile along with white of egg, if the instrument does not enter the eye due to its softness because some people have very hard eyes. You should pierce with it the conjunctiva only, without concentrating on the puncture. Rather, just touch the instrument's tip gently and then insert the instrument into what we have mentioned. And when you complete your work, prepare for the sleep by lying down firmly in a dark room.
He should abstain from all movements and coughing. You make his food whatever softens it naturally, and he should not move his head to the right or left whatsoever. And the bandage remains as is until the third day, then you take him into that dark room and try his sight.
You make him look at things, then you take off the bandage until the seventh day. And it is not suitable to do this during the treatment or after the puncture by your time, but rather one should avoid doing that before the water rises quickly with great vision.
If there is a hot ulcer, one should uncover the eye before the seventh day and correct that with something to calm the ulcer until it calms down. Then release his sight and put a cloth on his face to polish his sight from underneath for some days while he is in that dark room then.
He goes out of the house gradually and behaves in his causes, and know that the syringe cannot be dispensed with learned from observation several times Then he proceeds to work, and I have been informed by some Iraqis that he made a syringe in Iraq inflated, which absorbs water.
