The 24th Chapter.
For the treatment of flesh growing in the nose.
There may be different types of flesh growing in the nose, including something resembling many-legged scorpions and also carcinomatous flesh that is hardened and dark in color, and there may also be a type that is lean and not dark in color.
As for the lean flesh that is not malignant or cancerous, you should sit the patient in front of you facing the sun and have them open their nostrils and receive the needle into those fleshes then pull it out to the outside then cut off what you have grasped of it with a sharp pointed lancet from one side.
Until you know that the flesh is all gone, and what remains you were unable to cut off, then remove it with one of the gentle instruments carefully so that nothing remains. If blood flows or a hot swelling appears.
Then meet him with what is due, or if it was from the malignant tumors, hurry and cauterize until the bleeding stops and all the flesh disappears, then put in the nostril after cutting a powder of vinegar and water or a drink after that. If the nose opens up and moisture flows into the throat.
Know that he is cured, if moisture has not been carried out as it should, know that there are two gangrenous pieces inside him in the highest of the fractured bones which the instrument was unable to reach them. Then it is necessary for you to take a thread made from linen with some thickness.
And a knot is tied in it many times and between each knot, as much as a finger or less. The instrument pushes the tip of one thread into his nostril with a rod or what can be done after it is made like a needle, and pulls its breath until it reaches the trachea.
And it comes out on his neck and often this action is done by young boys in scribes and it is an easy matter for him who wills it. Then the two ends of the thread, one which came out of the mouth and the other which remained in the nostril are gathered together.
Then the meat is spread out by the knots which are in the thread, it does that until you know that the flesh has been cut by the knots of the thread. Then the thread is taken out and it remains in the nostril after wiping away the blood, a string that has been soaked in the Egyptian plaster is done like this for three days or more.
Until the plaster is eaten by everything that was left of the flesh. Then what remains in the nostril becomes a lead tube for days until he recovers, if he needs treatment it is dried and used like this.
And this is an image of the catheter by which the nostrils and medicines are poured into the nose:.
He puts from silver or copper, similar to a small candle, the plaster opened up like that.
And if you will make the tube closed like a pipe and the catheter's plaster flat.
It has a handle at its end as you see, it is grasped with if the grease or what you want from the instruments or the hanging things are heated in it.
Chapter Twenty-Five.
In the swellings that occur at the end of the nose.
Very often a boil occurs at the tip of the nose, it becomes large and increases with time until it disfigures its appearance.
And therefore it should be cut in its early appearance and all of it removed, then a poultice or the burning drug which is used instead of the poultice should be applied to the place. If cutting misses him until he becomes large, look if he was gangrenous and hard with little sensation.
Do not expose it to iron, for it is a cancerous tumor and I have often seen that when this tumor is cut, a large ulcer forms on the owner. And if the tumor is soft and has little sensation, and its color is not gangrenous, then I see that cutting it in its entirety can be done. Empty the boil and cut it without hesitation or delay, and treat the place with what dries and coagulates until it clears up.
Chapter Twenty-Sixth.
In the repair of the nose, cheek and ear. If its connection is severed due to an injury or the like, know that whenever a disconnection occurs in one of these membranes, little good can be done there except for some people.
So if one of them is presented, look, if the wound is wet with blood that you gather the edges of the wound with stitching and then treat it until it clears up. And if the disconnection has caused the edges to separate and each part is intact, then peel off each part with a thin layer of the visible skin until it rots.
Then gather the edges together with stitching and bind it, and sprinkle on it aloes and resin that have been ground up, and put on top of the dressing a sticky ointment made from oleated ointment or other adhesive ointments. And leave it tight for two or three days then take it off.
The medicine is changed and left until the threads are severed from themselves. Then, it is treated with ointment until it heals. The recipe for sewing is that the scattered connection be gathered either with needles as we described in sewing the belly or with thread as I have explained to you there.
The Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
In the removal of the swelling which appears on the lips.
Many people have small, hard swellings inside their mouths that resemble a cluster of grains. You should turn the lip and cut over each swelling then attach it to the hook.
And cut it from all sides, then stuff the place after cutting with powdered zinc until the bleeding stops. Then rinse with vinegar and salt and treat the places as is necessary until the wounds heal.
The Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
In cutting away excess flesh from the gum.
Often a lot of excess flesh grows on the gum, which the ancients called Abalus. You should attach it to a hook or hold it with a forceps and cut it at its origin and let the place bleed then put powdered zinc on the place.
Or one of the dried and adhesive growths. If that flesh returns after treatment, it often returns so cut it again and extract it because it does not return after being extracted.
The Twenty-Ninth Chapter.
In removing teeth with iron.
There may be rough and ugly scales on the surfaces of the teeth from inside and outside, between the gums. They may become discolored and green until they reach to the gum and uglify the teeth because of it.
You should sit the dentist in front of you with his head in your lap and extract the molar and tooth that show scales and things like sand until nothing is left, likewise do it for blackness, greenness, yellowness and other colors until it is clean.
If the filling in it has gone from the beginning of the alveolar ridge, then do to him a new alveolar ridge one day and another and yet another until you reach what you want. And know that the tooth needs an alveolar ridge with many forms according to what is prepared for your work.
In order that the alveolar ridge with which you fill the tooth from within may be different from the alveolar ridge with which you fill it from outside and that with which you fill between the teeth in another form, and these are many forms of filling that will all be prepared for you.
The Thirty-Third Chapter.
For extracting teeth.
You must treat the tooth from its root with every means and hesitate to extract it, for behind it is a noble essence even if it is not worth extracting.
Then if the surgeon decides to extract it, the tooth root should be firm in your hands until the tooth's root becomes suitable. Often the surgeon is deceived by the root and thinks it is in a healthy tooth, so he extracts it then the root does not go until the diseased tooth is extracted, for we have seen that done many times by the surgeons.
If the tooth root is firm in your hands, then it is necessary to girdle around the tooth with a forceps that has some strength until the gum covers it from all sides, then move it gently with your fingers or fine tweezers little by little until it loosens.
Then you can grasp it with the two strong forceps firmly and the head of the surgeon between your knees has been pressed down, does not move then pull the tooth straight out so that it is not broken. If it does not come out then take one of those instruments and insert it under him from all sides gently and turn him as you did first.
If the molar tooth is perforated or loose, it should be filled with a cloth and tightly sealed with a thin string so that it does not unravel when tightened with the ligature. It should be inspected around the gum from all sides.
You must be careful so that you do not break it, and a piece of it returns to the tooth again with a worse condition than the first one. And beware of doing what foolish dentists do, who attempt to bridge it without using what we have described.
They often inflict great injuries on people, such that it is more merciful for the tooth to break and for its roots to remain intact or some of them. Or it may loosen with some of the jawbone's bones, as we have seen, then be tampered with after loosening by wine or vinegar and salt; if there is bleeding from the place, then often this occurs when he has cut a piece of the gum and filled it with something.
If the gum did not help you, then take a ligature of soft string, the form of which to move the tooth first is long extremities and short handle, thick so that it does not bend when you grip with it on the tooth, and this is the form of the big ligatures:.
It will be as you see, thick at the handle so that if you grip it tightly it does not slip or bend, short at the ends. And let it be of Indian iron or forged steel, well-hammered at the ends and with some small teeth entering into each other; then grip with a firm and tight grip.
And it may be made so that its ends are like the shape of a rasp, and also have strong holding power.
The third chapter.
Concerning the removal of roots of teeth and extraction of broken bones of the jaw.
If the root of a tooth remains at the time of extraction and has broken, one should place a little fat on the spot for one or two days until it becomes relaxed. Then one enters (a thread) into it or a piece of cloth. The one that resembles the corners of the beak of the bird called al-barrajah. This is an image of the kalaib.
It would have been made like a file from inside or like an al-siklaif. If the extraction does not come out with this kalaib, one should drill into the root and expose all of the flesh with a probe, then enter the instrument which resembles a small handle, This is its image:
Short handled, a bit thick and not hollowed out so that it breaks. If the root comes out with this then otherwise use another instrument, whose image is this: the first one is triangular headed and has some thickness.
Another delicate triangular shaped image:
And we can also use this instrument with the two branches, and this is its image too.
And other instruments and pliers which are mentioned in the chapter on extracting teeth. And we can also use this instrument which resembles a large pincer, whose image is this:
Triangular headed, with some thickness a bit so that it does not break. And it should be hollowed out. Know that the instruments for extracting teeth are many and also all other instruments are numerous. The skillful craftsman by his craftsmanship may invent instruments according to what work and illness itself indicates to him.
Because among the diseases some were not originally equipped with instruments to differ in their kinds, if a bone from the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth has broken or decayed, then search for it in its place with one of these instruments and the kalaib that I mentioned in extracting roots.
We use this image as a model.
There should be some hardening in it so as to set the bone, lest it slips until the bone comes out. We then treat the place with the appropriate remedies, if there is some mild decay in the bone we remove its decay and corruption until it is clean, then we treat it until it heals.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
In the excision of tumours which are on top of others.
The tumours if they grow on top of their natural course are deformed by that shape, especially in women and slaves. It should be looked at; if the tooth had grown from behind another tooth.
But its removal was not possible or too late, then crush it. And if it is stuck to another tooth cut it with this tool as shown in the picture:.
It is similar to a small beak and it should be made of hard Indian steel with a very sharp tip. You can make an incision in the stone over several days due to its hardness so as not to disturb other teeth. And if it is movable and easy to remove, remove it using emery that will look like this:.
It is all made of emery and it is very fine, like the file with which needles are sharpened. It cools the tooth a little at a time over several days gently so that the tooth does not become dislodged and fall, then take hold of it again and remove it with some forceps.
And if a tooth has cracked and it is painful to the tongue when speaking, you should also cool it so that the discomfort of that crack goes away, becomes even and smooth, and does not cause pain to the tongue or spoil speech.
The Thirty-Third Chapter.
In splinting the movable teeth with silver threads or gold threads.
If an ancient abscess is presented, it trembles and moves with a blow or fall, nor can the surgeon bite on something that is eaten lest it be dropped. And I have treated them with adhesive medicines; thus treatment did not succeed in them.
But the trick in it is that you draw with a thread of gold or silver and gold is better because silver rusts and corrupts after some days, while gold remains forever without being exposed to that. And the thread should be intermediate in fineness and thickness as much as fits between the abscesses.
And the image of ligation is that you take the thread and insert its bend between the healthy teeth, then sew with the threads on both sides of the moving abscesses, whether one or more, until the stitching reaches to the healthy tooth from the other side.
Then you return the stitching to the side from which it started and hold your hand gently and wisely so that it does not move at all. And the hold of the thread should be at the roots of the abscesses lest it escapes, then cut the ends of the thread with scissors and join them together and twist them with a stick and hide them between the healthy tooth and the moving tooth.
So that the tongue is not irritated, then leave it like this bound until it remains so. If it dissolves or breaks, tighten it again with another thread and you will enjoy it thus for all eternity. And this is the appearance of abscesses and the ligation shape in two healthy teeth and two moving teeth as you see:.
And the single tooth or both may drop back into its place and be ligated as we have described and remain, and only a skilled craftsman can do that. And he may carve bone from cow's bones to make it like the shape of the tooth and put it in the place where the tooth has gone. And he binds as we said and it remains and he enjoys that.
The thirty-fourth chapter.
For cutting the ligament that is visible under the tongue in those who are unable to speak.
This ligament that is visible under the tongue may be either a natural one born with him or an adventitious one from a wound that has healed.
And the procedure in it is that you open the patient's mouth and hold his head firmly, then lift up his tongue and cut that nervous ligament with a razor until the tongue comes loose from its grasp. If there is some firmness and complexity in it resulting from the healing of a wound, then insert a probe into it and split it with the razor until the ligament becomes slack and the knot unravels.
And beware that the cut goes too deep and cuts a vein there, causing bleeding. Then apply compresses to the wound with rosewater or vinegar and cold water, then place a thread of linen under the tongue which the patient will hold in every night.
Lest it become adhered again. And if there is bleeding, put powdered alum on the place. And if the blood becomes strong, apply a pumice stone to the area as is suitable for that. Then treat him with the rest of the treatment until he recovers.
The thirty-fifth chapter.
For extracting a toad that has developed under the tongue.
There may be a swelling under the tongue resembling a small toad that prevents the tongue from performing its natural function, and perhaps even calcifies until it fills the mouth. And the procedure in it is that you open the patient's mouth facing the sun and look at the swelling.
And if you see it as swollen in color or black and hard, with the patient having no sensation of it, then do not handle him because it is cancer. And if it is inclined towards white and has moisture, then insert a probe into it and split it with a gentle lancet and free it from all sides.
If blood has flowed upon you during your operation, put over it a powdered alum until the bleeding stops. Then return to your work until you complete it, then rinse with vinegar and salt.
Then treat him by the remaining treatment suitable for that until he recovers.
Chapter Thirty-Sixth.
In the treatment of a swelling of the tonsils.
And what grows in the throat from other swellings may be exposed in the inside of the throat, glands resembling the glands that are exposed from outside called tonsils if you treated them with what I mentioned in the chapter they did not recover.
If the swelling is hard like a boil with little sensation do not touch it with iron and if it is red in color and its origin thick also do not touch it with iron, lest bleeding occur; but rather leave it alone until it ripens. It may either heal or burst open by itself.
And if it is white in color and curved, and its origin is thin, this one should be cut. The procedure for this is to examine before the operation whether its hot swelling has cooled down completely or decreased a little in decrease.
So when that, sit the surgeon in front of you with his back to the sun and his head near yours. Open his mouth and take a stick between your hands and compress his tongue downwards with this tool.
You make it from silver or copper, thin like a scalpel. If you compress the tongue with it and the swelling becomes apparent to you, put in the forceps and push them into the tonsil and pull it outwards as much as possible without pulling with it any of the peritoneum.
Then cut it with this tool, its shape resembles the scissors but its ends are curved and opposite to each other. Sharp very much, made from Indian iron or Damascus steel.
If this instrument is not available, then cut it with a sharp knife.
Sharp on one side, not sharp on the other. After cutting one stone, cut the other in this manner by itself, then after cutting it stir the instrument with cold water or vinegar and water.
If blood flow is revealed to him, stir with water in which the shells of almonds or the leaves of willow or similar things have been soaked until the bleeding stops, then treat it until he recovers. And sometimes tumors other than the two stones form in his throat, so cut them as was mentioned about cutting the stones, whether they are two or one.
And I have treated a woman with a tumor that had grown inside her throat, hitting the commissure lightly in sensitivity. It was about to block her throat and she was breathing through a narrow passage. The tumor had prevented her from eating and drinking water.
And she was on the verge of death if she had stayed for a day or two and the tumor had grown from it two branches until they protruded through her nostrils, so I quickly proceeded with the instrument. I inserted a hook into one of them then pulled it out, and a suitable piece came out with it.
Then I cut her where it protruded from the nostril, and I did that with what protruded from the other nostril. Then I opened her mouth and compressed her tongue, then inserted the hook into the same tumor and cut some of it off, and only a little blood flowed from it.
Then the woman's throat cleared and I proceeded to have her drink water, then she ate food. And after that we did not stop cutting away from that tumor for a long time, and the tumor left behind something in place of what was cut until it eventually healed with that.
So I cleared and removed the tumor from inside her throat and it stopped increasing. Then it migrated away and I don't know what Allah did with her afterwards.
Chapter Thirty-Seven
In cutting of the tumour of the thigh.
If a swelling occurs on the thigh which is called 'Amah, if it runs downwards and becomes inflamed and white and rectangular in shape then it is called 'Amd; and if it is thick and curved at the bottom it is called Ambeh; if it has been treated as mentioned in the chapter on division but the treatment was unsuccessful.
And I have seen the hot tumour to subside from it and be thin, so it should be cut; and if there is a lump that is curved and does not have length and is red or pale in colour or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
And there are many dangers to the patient, so if you see it in the shape I have mentioned, with its whiteness and length, then let the operator sit in the shadow of the sun, and compress his tongue with the instrument which is described later, and then insert a cauterizing iron into the Ambeh.
And pull it downwards and cut it with one of the instruments which are mentioned in cutting the stones, and you must not cut from it except what has increased the natural condition, without excess, because if you cut more from it you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after cutting, you use what we have described in cutting the stones and treat it until it heals; if the operator is afraid to cut it then you should resort to a trick without fear or caution, and the trick is that the patient's head should be put against your chest.
Then compress his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned, then take from the hot water which we mentioned in the chapter on the trick and mix it with a handful of unburned ash, and make it neither thick nor thin, and fill the instrument with this mixture, this is its shape:
Its end, where you put the medicine, is a cup like a teaspoon of mustard, and you place the instrument with the medicine on the thigh itself and the operator lies on his side so that saliva drips from it into his mouth so nothing comes out and hurts him.
Then grasp the hand with the drug and compress it on the patient for half an hour until you see that it has become blackened and numb from the bite of the drug. If you wish to take a thread, tear it apart and throw it into the drug.
And insert the thread into a tube from above so that it sticks to the patient, repeat this several times until you reach what you want of its thickness then leave it alone; it will become soft and crumble after three or four days. If you need to repeat the medicine, make it again.
After the thickening, wipe around the swelling with a thread soaked in fat and dry it with what is around it of medicine. Then moisten with cold water and treat from outside with poultices and from inside with catheters until it heals; for this type of treatment is more gentle than cutting and further away from fear.
And the patient can also be treated with what is softer than thickening and cutting, by treating with fumigation. Aloe, opoponax, mastic, myrrh, calamus, and similar herbs are taken, all of them or some of them are gathered together in a vessel and immersed in vinegar.
And it is boiled and the vessel, sealed with an earthenware lid, contains a hole in the middle of its covering. A device made from brass or copper is placed on top of it;
And the end with the aromatic resin is inserted into the mouth of the vessel until the steam rises to the patient through the tube until it calms down, yes. Then repeat this on her several times until she becomes soft, and beware that you make this treatment in the first occurrence of the swelling.
For it often increases in the swelling, and you should do that when her hot swelling subsides. And if you don't have this device, take a reed and place a eggshell crust on its end so that the vessel's mouth doesn't burn.
Because the membrane of the egg prevents the warmth of the vapor from burning the mouth, and this is a good treatment with safety.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
For the removal of thorns, and whatever sticks in the throat other than that.
Often a bone or thick thorn sticks in the throat, or something else of that kind; it should be removed by anything visible to the eye after compressing the tongue with the instrument at the sun.
So that you may see what is in the throat, and if it has not become visible to you and hidden in the throat, then the patient should vomit before he swallows his food into his stomach, perhaps the thing that stuck will come out with the vomiting or the patient will swallow a piece of lettuce leaf or a clove.
Or he will swallow a mouthful of dry bread or take a piece of soft sea sponge, then tie it into a thread and swallow it. If it reaches the place of the thorn, then pull the thread quickly; do that several times.
For often the thorn or bone becomes stuck in it and comes out, but if it does not come out as we mentioned earlier, then use a lead instrument like this:.
It will be a little thicker than a pipe, and at its tip it has a groove that the patient enters into with his tongue gently while lifting his head up and being careful not to touch his larynx so that he does not cough, and then pushes it in with the bone or thorn, or the physician puts it in with his hand.
And introducing the instrument into it is better because he knows the place of the stuck thing, and pushes it down or pulls with the instrument up; all that in a manner as far as he is prepared until it comes out.
Chapter Thirty-Nine.
For the removal of a molar that has stuck in the throat.
If you have treated the abscess with what we mentioned in the division from the treatment with medicine and it did not succeed, then look at the throat of the patient when the sun is out after compressing his tongue with the instrument that I described to you.
If your eye falls on the abscess, then grasp it with a small cauterizing iron or a gentle but firm cautery. If you are not able to do so, and otherwise, take a hollowed reed and insert it into the throat of the patient until close to the abscess, then insert an iron wrapped in fire into the cavity of the reed.
You do that several times and the patient abstains from water for a whole day, then he takes an earthenware vessel filled with cold water, opens his mouth into it and rinses with it without swallowing any of it, and moves the water sometimes after a while with his hand.
If the abscess has come out onto the spot if it has felt the water, and if it does not come out with what we have described, then gargle the throat with urine and with a warm paste made by the instrument that I described in the treatment of the boil. Do this several times, then it will come out.
And the method of the treatment in the caustic is that you take a vessel in which there is glowing hot iron made by fire, and the vessel is covered with a cloth having a hole in it. You place the end of the instrument into this hole then you pour the caustic, and put the patient's mouth on the end of the tube and close his mouth so that the caustic does not come out until he knows that the caustic has reached his throat.
If the abscess has come out onto the spot, if it does not come out and otherwise, then repeat the caustic several times, and let the patient abstain from drinking water and eat salty foods and garlic, he must come out with this treatment. And this is the form of the instrument which draws out the abscess from the throat if the eye falls on it.
She resembles the reeds as you see, except that she has this branching which enters into the throat and her extremities resemble the beak of a bird in its roughness if it touches something without leaving it:.
And another instrument which compresses the tongue is a wide iron ring as much as will suffice for the mouth above the tongue, it enters the mouth standing upright on its side and leaves the mouth open without the intention of the operator and he cannot pull it out at all until he removes it:.
The description of the instrument by which the mouth is opened to this measure.
Chapter Forty.
He makes a cut in the speech of the tumors and cuts them.
The tumors are many and varied in their speech and cut according to what is mentioned one by one in this book, and they differ in their interior and the moisture that they contain.
And the second kind is according to the places where they occur in the body, because the tumor occurring in the head is not like the tumor occurring in the buttocks and the tumor occurring in a place of flesh is not like the tumor occurring in a joint; each one has its own rule.
And among the tumors, it is not fitting to cut them unless after they have matured and become complete within them, and among them are those which should be cut even when they are fresh and still immature, like the tumors that occur close to the joints.
Because the tumor if it occurs close to a joint and its duration is long until it decomposes what surrounds it may corrupt the ligaments or nerve of that joint, thus being the cause of atrophy of that member or the tumor being close to a main organ.
Because if you delayed cutting it until it matures, you would harm the main organ or it is close to the buttocks so cut it fresh and not fully mature, but only the tumor that occurs close to the buttocks because if the pus decomposes it will penetrate inside the buttocks and become a suppuration.
There occurs in a certain case, which does not heal, one should know the times of the abscesses that may have matured when the abscess is calm and its pain has gone down and the fever has departed and there has been a decrease in redness and swelling and the pulsation at the head of the abscess and all other signs.
It should be inserted into the lower part of the abscess if possible, in order to make it easier for the pus to flow downwards or into a more superficial and firmer place within the abscess; and the catheter should be passed throughout the body if the abscesses are located near the hands and feet.
And in the places of the muscles and tendons and nerves and vessels in general, and in all the flat places that have no bend to them; but as for those which are bent then the catheter should be passed according to this place; and if the abscess is in a bloody location it is best to leave the catheter out.
Until its maturation is complete as we mentioned, you should not catheterize it before that; for if you do then the discharge from it will flow slowly and be full of sediment and filth, and perhaps its edges may harden and its mouth may become obstructed. And some abscesses are catheterized on the surface of the body when necessary or according to what the part needs.
It should be used in small abscesses with a single catheter and in large abscesses with a wide catheter or several incisions according to the size of the abscess; and there may be some abscesses that require the skin to be scraped and cut if it has become like a rag.
It becomes in some cases like one that has died, as is seen in many gangrene and abscesses; from it some are incised with a three-cornered cut, and from others a cut is made resembling the shape of an aspen leaf.
Among them is that in which the round incision and crescentic incision, and similar cuts are made; and if it has no head like smooth flat tumors, then a small poultice should be applied to it only, and if the tumor is large and has accumulated much pus and its pustules have formed, one should not hasten to apply (the poultice) lest all the pus come out at that time.
But rather take some of it out and then apply a poultice to the tumor until another day, and then take out some pus also; do this repeatedly in succession until all of it comes out.
And especially if the patient is weak in strength or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man, for often the vital spirit resolves along with the sudden exit of pus and so the patient may die without you realizing it; beware this matter extremely.
And after applying the poultice to these tumors, you should dress and observe; if the wound of the tumor is small or the incision is one simple cut, then use a lint from flax or fine cotton. And if the tumor is large and there were many cuts of the poultice.
Then you should insert a thread into each cut so that some of them reach one another; and if the tumor has had part of it cut off or scraped, then you should stuff it with fine cotton or linen fluff without moisture and bind it until the third day.
Then you should remove it and treat it with what is necessary of ointments until it heals; if bleeding appeared on the site during your treatment, then use cold water and vinegar after having a linen cloth steeped in them and applying it to the site of the bleeding repeatedly.
If the bleeding continued, then you should use the treatment and medication and cauterizations which we have mentioned in many places of this book and in the section; and if it were winter time and the place of the tumor was rich with nerves, then you should wet the poultice with wine and hot oil.
She places it on the site, and if it is in summer and the sites are bloody, then she should carry the ointment drunk with water and oil or with wine and oil; all of that cold until the third day as we said, then the abscess will break and be drained.
She uses in its treatment whatever she thinks is needed until it heals, this is what she needs to know for the treatment of abscesses in general and as for the detailed method then I have mentioned each abscess how its way to be treated clearly.
The Forty-First Chapter.
For the incision on abscesses which appear on the skin of the head.
There are small abscesses on the skin of the head, and they are a type of pustules that contain pus, it is like a hen's nest with conditions, and there are many types of them; some fatty and some containing moisture similar to dung.
And there is also what contains moisture similar to blood and soup, and like that; and some of them are hardened and solidified, and all of them do not have a danger in cutting her and removing it if you are not confronted with a vein when cutting her.
And the work in cutting her is that you scratch it first with a tool that comes in the shape after this one which is called the "madss", until you know what it contains; if it contains moisture, then cut it longitudinally with a small incision on its surface:.
And start with the cut from line ~b~ to line ~j~, if the moisture is discharged then scrape off the sac that was containing that moisture and cut it completely, do not leave anything at all; often it will return if there is something left.
Then dip a thread in the ointment if it is available, otherwise in salt water and fill with it the wound, and leave it for another day; because it will eat what remains of the sac. Then repeat on it the thread again and again as you need to.
Until you have made certain that nothing remains of the cyst, then treat the wound with ointments until it heals. And if the swelling contains fatty matter, cut it as follows:
Cut with a scalpel and open the sinews on either side of the wound and remove it from all sides, exert yourself in removing the membrane that contains it. If an artery obstructs you, do as I have described to you afterwards, and also do in the swelling if it is hardened from the cut.
The treatment is as I have mentioned, and cutting into the hardened swelling is easier because it has little blood and moisture. And sometimes these swellings that are in the head of some people have no moisture at all; which is why I cut into one.
The head of an old woman, I cut into the swelling which was like a hard flint, white and hard to the extent that if anyone had thrown it would have shattered; and the other swellings that occur on the heads of children were not like this.
And when the swelling is under the ears, cut it all with a simple incision and make its base lower so that the matter may flow down more easily, then treat it in accordance with what suits it.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
In cutting on pigs which occur in the neck, these swellings often occur in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin and can occur throughout the body; and what occurs in the neck among them is one or more.
And each pig among them will be in a special sac inside it, as with the fatty matter and swellings of the head which we have described; and there are many kinds of these pigs, some hardened, some containing moisture, and some malignant that do not respond to treatment.
What I have seen of this condition is, in touch, a good state and it is near to the colour of the skin; it moves towards every direction without being connected with the nerve of the neck or the diaphragm or artery nor was it swollen. It should be cut with a simple incision from above to below the body in this form from line ~j~ to line ~b~:.
And it should be peeled from all sides and the skin flaps should be sutured with a needle or two needles or many needles as we said for head ulcers; it is brought out little by little and it is on the neck not to cut a vein or a nerve and the surgeon should not be very sharp.
Lest your hand increase the cuts or the patient become alarmed, so you cut what is not needed to be cut; if you cut a vein or artery and it prevents you from working, put some powdered alum or some of the powders that stop bleeding in the wound.
Then sew up the wound and leave it until the swelling subsides and the wound calms down and dries; when the bleeding stops at that time, return to your work until you finish; then search with your forefinger if there is any left; then take out small pieces of meat as much as possible and cut them into pieces and clean them.
If there is a large artery in the centre of the sow, it should not be cut from its root but rather it should be tied with a double and tight thread and left until it falls out by itself without being harmed; then stuff the wound with cotton wool that has been soaked in the Egyptian ointment and then treat it.
And if you cut the whole sow, it should be sewn up and stitched from its armpit after you have known that there is no discharge left; if you see that there has been a considerable amount of discharge because of the size of the sow.
You should aim to cut it from its root and base, and make use of stitching and what we mentioned. And if it is a pig that has retained moisture, then bind it with a thin layer of dough where its cooked part appears to you, and place the dough below as we said.
Then you should use the poultice after applying the fatty ointment, similar to it, so that what remains of corruption may be eaten until you see the wound has cleansed. Then treat it with the plant-based ointments for flesh until it heals.
The 43rd Chapter.
In a cut of the throat from a tumor occurring inside the gullet.
The ancients have mentioned this cut in the throat and I have not seen anyone in our country make it, and this is in accordance with their speech. But as for those suffering from stricture, they should avoid cutting the throat, because it will not benefit them.
So that all the trachea and lungs may become dry, but as for those who have a hot tumor in the mouth or throat or tonsils, if it is not an affliction in the windpipe, then cutting of the throat should be used to escape from the harm which will be from choking.
So if we wish to do that, then we should cut the trachea under three circles of the windpipe's circles or four small cuts in width between two circles as much as the cut would be in the peritoneum not in the pleura and this place is suitable for cutting.
Because it is not fleshy and the blood vessels are far from it, so if the physician is timid then he should take the mucous membrane of the gullet with forceps then cut the skin until when it reaches the windpipe, avoid the blood vessels if he sees any.
Then he should cut the peritoneum as we have described, and take hold of the cut windpipe from the phlegm that comes out of it with what cracks and discontinuation of voice. And leave the wound open for a time until the danger of choking passes, then bring together the edges of the wound with skin.
He wrote it down alone, without connective tissue. Then the remedies are used which make the flesh grow until it heals. The author of this book said that the meaning of what we have written is if they saw a string closing one of these tumors mentioned.
And when the patient is on the brink of death and he himself thinks to have his throat cut so that the patient takes a few breaths and escapes from death, but they are ordered to leave the wound open until the disease is cleared up and its term is three days or so.
So then they were ordered to sew up the wound and treat it until it heals, and I myself have seen a maid take a knife and she had him cut some of her bronchus with it, so I was called to treat her but I found her in bad condition like one who has been slaughtered, so I uncovered the wound.
I found the blood that came out of the wound to be small, so I was certain that she had not cut a lung or an artery, and the breath was coming out of the wound, so I examined her further and I sewed up the wound and treated it until she healed, and nothing was left for the maid but a hoarseness in her voice.
And she returned to her best condition after some days, so from here we say that cutting the throat has no danger in it.
The Fourth and Forty-Fourth Chapter.
Concerning the incision on the swelling that appears in the larynx from outside and is called "fillah" of the larynx.
This swelling which is called "fillah" of the larynx can be a large swelling on the color of the body and it is common in women, and there are two types.
It is either a natural one or an acquired one, as for the natural one, there is no remedy for it, and as for the acquired one, it can be of two types, one resembling fatty tumors and the other resembling a swelling that occurs from a tangled vein, and in its incision there is danger. Do not expose it to iron at all, unless you find a small one within and search for it with the probe, when you have found it and made its edges resemble fatty matter and it was not connected to any vessels, then cut it as you would cut fat. And take them out with what they contain from the sac if it is in a sac; otherwise, search for all of them and then treat the place as needed.
The Forty-Fifth Chapter.
On cutting into types of fat.
The fats are of many kinds and all their types have been mentioned in the classification; it is necessary to mention here the difference between fat and abscess, as the latter is an inflammation, I say that an abscess will be accompanied by heat, fever and severe pains until the pus comes out. It becomes putrid and then the fever and heat subside; but fat does not come with any heat or fever or pains, and it is contained in a membranous sac which is its special envelope and which is of the same color as the body, and it begins like a mustard seed and becomes larger and smaller.
And it is of two kinds, either fatty or containing moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many as mentioned in the classification; so if you come to treat the fat, first search for it and inspect it with a probe called medsas as its shape will appear in the chapter preceding this.
Measure the size of the tumor, then take out the probe and look at what comes out in its place; if fluid of any color comes out, cut it with a small incision as mentioned in other tumors; and if no fluid comes out after taking out the probe, know that it is fatty.
Cut it with a deep incision on this shape as I have shown you, and hang it with the forceps; then remove the skin from all sides gently and preserve it in a sac if you are able to extract it sound along with the fat.
If the pouch burst open while working and it could not be removed properly, that often happened. Remove it piece by piece until nothing remains from it; for it is common for a little or much substance to remain in such cases.
If a small amount remains and it becomes swollen, then suture the wound with some sharp needles when you are finished, cover it with something to calm the hot swelling and treat it with all remedies until it heals. If the substance is large, cut the sides of the pouch and treat it as a gaping wound.
If a vein bursts, whether it is a main one or not, and there is a risk of bleeding, you must act quickly; fill the place with powdered alum and leave it clamped for two or three days until the wound cools down and the flow of blood ceases then return to cutting what remains of the substance.

The Forty-Seventh Chapter.
In the swelling of the breast of men.
Which resembles the breast of women. It may become swollen in some people at the peak of passion so that it resembles the breast of women and remains warm and ugly, therefore, whoever dislikes this should cut into the breast with a crescent-shaped incision in this shape.
From line ~b~ to line ~j~:. Then cut out all the fat, then fill the wound with a medicinal unguent, and sew up the lips of the wound with stitching and treat it until it heals. If the breast falls below and relaxes into its bone as is shown to women.
Therefore, it should be cut into its upper parts with two incisions resembling a crescent shape, each of them connected to the other at their ends so that the larger line encircles the smaller one in this shape:. From line ~b~ to line ~j~, then remove the skin in between the incisions, and take out the fat, and use what was mentioned from stitching and drills, and whatever treatment is needed until it heals.
If you did not understand the cuts that are necessary for you to make because of the sharpness of the tool or because of bleeding, it should be stuffed into the wound with cotton soaked in a strong ointment and left until what remains of fat is eaten, then treat it until it heals.
The Forty-Eighth Chapter.
In the swelling under the armpit.
These growths under the armpit are of a firm pigmented type enclosed in a sac and some contain fluid. As for those that contain fluid, they should be incised with an elliptical cut like this.
From the line ~b~ to the line ~j~, if all that is in the tumor has been drained, then close it with linen and leave until another day, then remove the thread.
It is treated with the suitable ointment until it heals. If the tumor is of the type of pigmented nodules, then incise it as we mentioned in relation to cutting the nodule, regardless, if the wound extends so that the discharge becomes excessive, then use a poultice as we mentioned previously.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
In cutting the tumor that is exposed by the artery or vein and which is called aneursma.
If the artery is cut and the skin above it adheres, a tumor often appears as a result of that, and also an effusion or swelling often appears in the vein.
And the signs by which it is recognized that the tumor and effusion are due to an artery or a vein, if the tumor is from the artery then it will be a flat one gathered in the depth of the body, and if you push the tumor with your finger, you will feel it as if it has a hair.
And if it is from the vein, then the tumor will be curved in the outer part of the body. The incision on these tumors is dangerous, especially those that are in the armpit, elbow and neck and in many other places in the body, and they were very large; so one should avoid treating them with iron.
And also, what is found in the extremities or in the head should be avoided. As for that which is an intumescence from a blood vessel, make an incision in the skin along its length, then widen the incision with probes, then dissect the vessel and free it from the fasciae.
Until it is uncovered, then a needle is introduced beneath it and it is pushed to the other side and the artery is tied with a thread of two thicknesses at the place I mentioned as one of the places where the two arteries are sutured. Then bleeding is stopped by applying a compress on the spot between the ligatures until all the blood in it comes out.
And the swelling is resolved, then the treatment that produces a discharge is used until the ligatures are shed, and it is treated with ointments suitable for that until it heals.
If the swelling is before a cut of the vein, it is necessary that you take hold with your hand what you can from the swelling along with the skin, then a needle is introduced below the place where you took hold with your hand and pushed through it with a thread of two thicknesses until it comes out on the other side. Then the swelling is tied with a good knot according to what I mentioned to you in tying the spongy ligament from both sides of the thread, if you fear that the threads will slip then another needle is introduced with another thread under all the swelling at the point of intersection of the first needle.
And tighten your threads in four places, then cut the swelling in the middle until what is inside it comes out, and cut the excess skin leaving what remains of it tied. Then place a poultice that you have moistened with wine and oil on it. Then the treatment is used which is with ointments and plasters until it heals.
The Fiftieth Chapter.
In the swelling that results from a nerve twist.
Just as swelling occurs in the vein and artery, so also does swelling occur in the nerve if a blow or excessive fatigue has occurred or something similar to it, and it is more likely to happen at the places of the elbows and the loins.
In every place where the joints move, and it is a swelling which resembles the color of the rest of the body, and most often it does not hurt, if one presses firmly on it he feels tenderness in it, like numbness, and it is not gathered together inside the body.
But it may be under the skin and moves to every direction, and does not go forward or backward. Whatever of it is in the joints should not be treated with iron, for it may cause inflammation, and whatever of it is in the head or on the forehead.
Cut the skin with a lancet, and if the swelling is small, grasp it with forceps and cut it from its origin. And if it is large, cauterize it with an iron cautery and remove it, then stitch up the wound and treat him until he recovers.
The 52nd Chapter.
In cutting abscesses that are exposed in the abdomen.
There are many abscesses in some people's abdomens and other parts of their bodies that are called "futriyah" because of their resemblance to a fungus. Its root is thin and its head is thick, the edges of which have become swollen, and it may be small or very large.
And I have seen a man with two growths in his abdomen, resembling the most things fungus-like, white and thin at their roots, which had become swollen and ruptured, and liquid was always oozing from them. I cut them off and threw them on the scale: one of them weighed around eighteen dirhams, and the other around six.
And the operation in cutting them is to inspect, if the abscess is wet and the colour of the growth is white and damp, thin at its root, cut it off with a broad lancet, and have a mortar near you containing hot water, for often much blood will flow out when cutting.
Then, if a vein bursts and it becomes swollen, then if you see the cut from iron being cowardly in pain, take a strong lead thread and tie it to the swelling that has this description, leave it for two days, then add force to tighten the lead so that it continues to be tight.
Whenever you exert pressure on the swelling until it bursts and falls out by itself without any difficulty, then if the swelling is thick in origin its cutting causes some fear and danger, especially when it's in the abdomen; but half or part of it can be cut.
Then tighten it so that it doesn't come back, then treat it until the wound heals, and beware of exposing a swelling that is pale in color, little sensitivity, ugly appearance; for it is a sign of cancerous tumour, and we will mention cancer after this.
The Second Chapter Fifty-Two.
In the treatment of carbuncle.
The carbuncle is from many causes, either the perforation of the omentum which is on the belly and comes out from it pus or matter as what appears in all abscesses, or blood that flows from a vein or artery as has been mentioned before, or a pustule erupts underneath.
If it is from the perforation of the omentum and the coming out of pus, then the colour of the tumour will be similar to the colour of the body, and it will be smooth and without pain, and its position will become clear. And if it is from the coming out of matter, then its position will be as we described with a great difference, so if you press it with your fingers it disappears and then returns, and perhaps there is a cracking sound and it becomes very large when entering the bath and experiencing severe fatigue. And if it is because of humidity, then it will be smooth.
It does not disappear when you press it with your hand, and it does not increase or decrease. And if it is because of blood, then with these signs the tumour appears black. And if it is from a fatty growth, then the tumour will be hard and firm and will remain in one place.
If it was caused by the wind, his touch is gentle. The procedure for that is to look at him. If the swelling of the abscess has been caused by blood from an artery or a vein or the wind, one should refrain from treating him. For there will be fear and congestion in that case, as I informed you in the chapter which I mentioned concerning tumours produced by arteries and veins.
If the swelling of the abscess has been caused by a bowel or intestine, one should order the patient to grasp himself and stand upright with his intestines extended, then apply lint around the whole swelling. Then order him to lie on his back before you, then apply a broad lancet around the swelling in the place where you instructed with lint, then push into the midst of the tumour up as far as with a large needle, then tie the place of the application with strong thread or linen binding tightly.
And the knot of the bandage will be a tuck, then open up the compressed part of the tumour above the bandage and insert your left thumb into it and seek for the intestine. If you find it, it has been taken by the bandage, so loosen the tucks and push the intestine back inside the belly. And if you find an intestine, stretch it out with a needle.
And cut off the redundant part. If an artery or vein obstructs you, bind it with a cloth and return to your work. Take two needles and insert strong threads into them, then insert the needles into the ligature which you made around the swelling, threaded, then pull on the tumour in four places on the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the place until the compressed flesh putrefies and falls off by itself or it is cut if it becomes gangrenous. Then treat it with what needs to be of ointments until it heals, if the swelling of the abscess was caused by festering meat inside.
If it is moistened [inside the abscess], it should be constricted as we have said, and the blood or moisture found in it should be extracted, then treated with what unites the place.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
In the treatment of cancer.
We have mentioned in the categorization the types of cancer and how it should be treated with medication, and we warned against treating it with iron lest it become ulcerated, and we mentioned cancer that has arisen in the womb and warned about its treatment.
The ancients have mentioned that if the cancer is in a place where it can be completely removed, such as one that has arisen in the breast or thigh and similar movable parts, then it should be taken out with its root, especially when it is small and recent. But if it is advanced, it should not be approached.
I have not been able to cure anyone of it, and I have not seen any other who has reached that point. The treatment in such a case is, as we said, to advance [the abscess] until the pus bursts out several times, then to drain it if it is located in the veins with a clear filling.
Then [the surgeon] should lay the pus in a bandage, allowing it to heal, then insert into the cancer suitable probes, and constrict it from all sides along with the skin, investigating until nothing remains of its roots. Then let the blood flow without cutting it quickly.
But instead, compress the place and drain all the thick blood with your hand or whatever instruments you can, even if in working on it a large amount of bleeding occurs from cutting an artery or vein; stop the flow of the blood until it stops, then treat it with other treatment until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Fourth.
In the treatment of carbuncle.
We have been told in the division about kinds of dropsy and how water gathers, and signs of each type and its treatment with drugs. The one which is treated with iron is only the kind of edema and does not approach by iron the kind of boils or the fleshly type at all.

Cough or diarrhea and the like then beware not to treat it with iron for that would be foolishness. If you see the disease strong in power, not having another sickness besides the boil alone, and it is neither a child nor an old man then do in this case to prepare the iron in front of you standing upright. And a servant behind him presses his belly with his hands and pushes the water down towards the backside then take a pointed lancet like this:.
Pointed on both sides long and with a defined end like a lancet but it has some curvature slightly so as not to leak when working towards the intestines and thus harm him then immerse if the boil arose from the direction of the intestines.
You must cut with the lancet from the navel by three fingers downwards following it above the backside, if the boil arose because of liver sickness then let your incision be shorter than the navel by three fingers. If it arose because of spleen sickness then let the incision in the right side be by three fingers.
Also the incision should not be on the side which the patient wants to lie on lest the pus trickle onto that weak place, then puncture all of the skin with the instrument and insert the instrument into that incision and raise your hand.
With the instrument between the skin and the membrane, as if you were stripping it off. The size of what you are peeling should be like a nail or similar to it. Then puncture the membrane until the instrument reaches an empty place which is a location of water. Then take it out and insert into the hole the tool that its shape is shown here.
And it is like a tube from a thin rod made of brass or copper or from smooth and polished horn. At the bottom of it there is a small hole, and on its sides two holes, one from each side as you see.

At its upper end there is a ring. If the instrument reaches the water, then it will descend on the instrument, and thus suck up from the water in that time an intermediate amount because if you sucked out from it more than what should be at the time perhaps the patient would die due to the collapse of his vital spirit.
Or it may make him faint and close to death, but suck from it an amount according to his strength, and what indicates the condition of the patient with the strength of his pulse and the good color of his complexion. Then take out the instrument and stop the water, that is, it will be retained in its container.
Because of the skin which covers the hole in the membrane, which I told you to plug up in that manner. Then use the instrument again on another day if you see the patient capable of that.
And also take out from the water a small amount. Do that for some days while you are on his back and be cautious not to make a mistake, so that there remains only a little water. If it is lightened on the patient and you left much of the water, then treat him with burial in hot sand.
And have him sweat a lot in the bathhouse and the sun, and sprinkle him with salt to quench his thirst and treat him with dried medicines until he recovers. And feed him so that it goes into his stomach, liver, and spleen after draining the water as I described before this.
Chapter Fifty-One.
In the treatment of children who are born with their urethral orifices either not perforated or narrow or in a wrong place.

With a thin needle like this:
Then one puts a thin lead pin in the hole, ties it and holds it for three or four days until the urine has pushed it away and falls out, then returns it; and if the lead is not put in, it may be that the urine which flows onto the place will not let it close.
And as for those whose urethral orifice is narrow, it is treated with lead as we mentioned for a long time until it expands; and as for those among them in whom the opening is in the wrong place, that is, some are born with the opening at the end of the penis so they cannot urinate forward.
Until it lifts the penis with his hand upwards and it is unable to urinate forward, this being a very bad reason; and the procedure for that is that the patient lies on his back.
Then you extend the penis with your left hand as far as possible and make a cut in the head of the penis with a razor or a sharp lancet, like an awl or if it were to be sculpted into something with its middle directed forward similar to the penis, and the hole should come out in the middle where it is supposed to.
And be careful with bleeding when you are doing this, as it often happens; so counteract it by cutting the blood and treating the wound until it heals.
Chapter Sixty-Sixth.
In the case of an abscess which is formed in the skin, penis and scrotum and testicles, and when the skin adheres to the penis.
This swelling often appears in the urethra, and it is a boil-like abscess that may be foul or not foul. What is not foul should be tied with a gentle string.

If the swelling is in a scrotum that has not been circumcised, and some of it is inside and some of it is outside, then you should remove the part that is inside first until it becomes suppurated. Then treat it from the outside.
Because if you treat them together, the scrotum may perforate. It can also appear in women and in the scrotum as blackness and corruption. So you should cut off all that has turned black and seemed to corrupt or has corrupted.
Then apply honey with ground and pounded cloves and kermes on it, then treat him with the rest of the treatment until he heals. If there is an appearance of bleeding, use vinegar with a halved copper cauterizer in this way:
The vinegar is useful for both cases, meaning bleeding and wound if it corrupts. If the membrane becomes hardened and suddenly goes away at a certain time, then you should insert a lead tube into the male member to pour the acid on it. And as for the scrotum being stuck to the membrane.
And this adhesion occurs in him whose scrotum is healthy and he has not been circumcised, and it may appear to be stuck together beforehand due to a wound or a tumor. So you should scrape it off with a moist sponge until the bond breaks and the membrane is freed from all sides.
If the identification of them is difficult during examination, it should be peeled off something from the sheath and from the covering; for the covering is thin so perhaps it will burst quickly due to its thinness. Then separate between the covering and the sheath with a fine linen cloth that has been moistened in cold water lest they also adhere together.
Then he treats it with astringent wine until it heals.
The 47th Chapter.
For the cleansing of boys and the treatment of what afflicts them from errors.
The circumcising is not other than the disruption of connection like other incisions, except that since it was from our action by will and its use in boys especially, it is necessary to make the best effort in this.
And the easier path leading to safety. I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books because it was not used in their laws, but rather it is what we have acquired.
Through experience and because I found that the majority of artisans and barbers use purification with a file and scissors, and they use ligatures with thread and cuts with knives, and I have tried all these forms.
So I did not find better than purifying with scissors and tying with thread, because purification with a file often finds difficulty in it because the skin of the covering is double-layered so perhaps the upper layer of skin is cut while the lower layer remains.
He is forced to cut again and repeated pain, and purification with forceps does not guarantee cutting off the end of the urethra because it may enter its hole, and as for purifying with a knife then perhaps the skin would slough and spoil your work or the boy's skin is short by nature.
For often they are born in that state and do not need purification, which I have seen. And as for purifying with scissors and tying with thread, experience has shown me its superiority because the blade of the scissor cuts to match the upper blade as the lower blade.
When you cut your finger with the scissors in harmony so that they are both cutting at the same length and time, then the cord will become like a partition wall to the skin of the anal canal from all sides without making any mistake, and the intention of the work is first to imagine the anus.
And especially if the person who understands a little knows that you tie the thread only in his anus and leave him for another day then let it out and set it loose on every side you can do that to him and he will accept it with his mind, then stop it between your hands standing upright.
And he should not be sitting and hide the scissors in your armpit or under your foot so that the eye of the anus does not fall on it at all nor on anything of the tools, then put your hand into his anus and blow on the skin and scrape it upwards until the head of the anal canal comes out.
Then purify what gathers in it from dirt then tie the taught place with a doubled thread then tie below it slightly a second band then grasp with your thumb and index finger the place of the lower band firmly and cut between the two bands. Then raise the skin upwards quickly and take out the head of the anal canal then let the blood flow a little it is better and less for an anal abscess then dry him with a damp cloth then sprinkle on him from cold, dry ashes of burned oak it is best I have tried or accurate in cauterization it is also excellent.
Then raise the skin upwards quickly and take out the head of the anal canal then let the blood flow a little it is better and less for an anal abscess then dry him with a damp cloth then sprinkle on him from cold, dry ashes of burned oak it is best I have tried or accurate in cauterization it is also excellent. Then carry on the cauterization from above with a cloth moistened by beaten egg in rose water mixed with liquid rose petal then leave it on him for another day then treat him with the rest of the treatment until he recovers.
And this is the image of the scissors that is suitable for cleaning:.
It will be straight cutting scissors without a bend in them with the wire fasteners and the length of the blades will be equal to the length of the handles, as for the mistake that occurs in cleaning perhaps the inner skin will be all or some of it turned inside out when cut so you should extend it from your time with your fingernails before the place becomes swollen.
If you cut it evenly, but you are not able to hold it firmly with your fingers, then grasp it with tweezers and cut it. If for three days following this the swelling under the head of the armpit remains swollen and warm, leave it until the hot swelling subsides and then remove it gently.
Cut it according to what is prepared for you, and be cautious from the head of the armpit; if a part of the head of the armpit is cut, it does not harm that. Heal the wound with what cures wounds, that which we described in the article on boils.
And if a part of the skin above it is cut and contracted upwards, it will not harm that either. Heal it with what we mentioned until it clears up.
Chapter 48.
In the treatment of urine obstructed in the bladder.
Urine obstructed in the bladder is due to its blockage from stone, or solid blood, or mucus, or fatty tissue that has grown and similar things. If you treat this with what we mentioned, varieties of treatment described in the classification.
And if the urine has not been released and you see that its blockage is from a stone which has moved into the neck of the bladder, then it becomes necessary for the doctor to sit on his knees and have another man ride him like a camel, with his stomach towards his back, and grasp the stone as much as possible.
At that point the neck of the bladder is forced to push the stone behind and the urine will be released. If this does not work as mentioned and the condition becomes severe on the doctor, it becomes necessary to use a device called catheter which its image is shown:.
It is made from silver and it is thin, smooth and curved like the tube of a bird's feather in the shape of an S. It is long about a finger's breadth and a half and has a small beak at its top. The end used for drawing out urine is taken with a bent thread and tied tightly with a wool or cotton string.
You insert the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe and plug it with a stopper if any wool remains so that it enters the tube tightly, then smear the syringe with oil or fat or egg white and sit the needle on a chair.
She blows into the bladder and urethra with wet poultices or oil and warm water, then inserts the syringe gently into the urethra until it reaches its root, then bends the urethra upwards towards the navel and pushes the syringe inside.
Until the urethra is bent then the syringe is pushed inside until it reaches close to the bladder seat, the man leans down and the syringe inside him, then pushes him until he reaches the bladder and feels the needle has reached something empty.
This is done in this order because the urethra through which the urine flows has a curvature, then the thread with wool is pulled out strongly for a little bit so that the urine follows the wool, then it is taken out and the urine is drained, and the syringe is repeated.
She continues to do that until the bladder is emptied and the needle finds ease.
The 58th chapter.
How to inject the bladder with cathartics.
And the image of the tools that are suitable for this, made from brass or polished ivory, having a long tube on a handle to pour in water and medicine, which is called the cathartic and here is its picture:.
It is made from polished brass or ivory, having a long tube on a handle that is polished all except the end which has three holes, two of them are one side and one of them is the other side as you see.
The empty place where the two reservoirs are, according to as much as it fills them, until if you draw with it something from moisture it is drawn and if you press with it it moves forward like what the naddaha makes that oil is thrown in sea wars.
If you want to pour the moisture into the bladder, then put the end of the syringe in the moisture and draw with the reservoir up; the moisture will be drawn inside the syringe. Then insert the tip of it into the urethra as we described earlier for the catheter, then push the moisture out by the reservoir.
For that moisture will reach the bladder in its place until it is felt by the patient. And here is a picture of another syringe, which also catheterizes the bladder.
It is made from brass or lead, its upper part resembles the small tube and below it a loop where the strap falls in. Then take the bladder skin and put into it the moisture you want to catheterize the bladder with, then tie it between the two reservoirs tightly with doubled thread.
And heat that moisture a little on the fire, then put the tip of the syringe into the urethra, then grasp your hand tightly onto the bladder with the moisture strongly until the patient feels that moisture has reached the bladder.
If you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of leather and make a circle from it, puncture it all over its circumference. Then put a tight thread into the hole as you rotate it, and gather the circle together like how you gather clothing after you put what you want from moisture, dyes and water inside it.
Then tie it to the machine and do with it as you did with the bladder, make a hole for your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
The 60th chapter.
In the extraction of stones.
We have mentioned in the classification the types of stones and their treatment with medicine, and we have pointed out the difference between those that are formed in the kidneys and those that are formed in the bladder, along with the signs thereof, and also we have mentioned the stone in which surgical intervention is carried out by hand and incision.
And it is the stone that occurs in the bladder especially and which lodges in the urethra, and I am describing this clearly and briefly.
I say that the stone formed in the bladder is more commonly encountered in children, and one of its signs is that the urine comes out from the bladder like water in its quantity.
And in it (the bladder) sand is visible, its presence felt and played with, and often it protrudes and spreads with it the prepuce in many of them. The urination of boys becomes easy from it until they reach fourteen years, and it becomes difficult for the elderly. As for the young men, it is intermediate between that.
And what is his stone greater will be its treatment easier, and the smaller, contrary to that. So if we resort to treatment, it should first inject the medicine through a catheter which comes out all the urine that is in his bladder because it may prevent the presence of the stone when examined.
Then the instrument is taken with him and pulled downwards so that the stone comes down to the neck of the bladder, or it is shaken from a high place several times. Then he is made to sit facing you standing up with his hands under his thighs so that the whole bladder tilts downwards then it is searched for.
And then you search for it from the outside. If I feel the stone in the space, then hasten with your hand to cut into it. And if it does not fall down at once, then take a drop of oil from the left hand, and if he is a boy use the little finger, and if an adult use the middle finger.
If the patient is an adult, then you should insert a catheter into his bladder and search for the stone until it falls under your finger. Then you move it little by little to the neck of the bladder. Then you press on it with your finger and push it out towards the place you want to cut.
And you command a servant to compress the bladder with his hand. And you command another servant to extend his right hand towards the top and with his other hand extend the skin under the perineum towards the place where the cut will be, then take the curved scalpel which is shown in this figure:
And you cut in between the scrotum and the perineum, not in the middle but beside the left iliac prominence. And the cut is along the same line as the stone and your finger in the scrotum pressing it to come out. The cut is from outside wide and narrow from inside according to what allows the stone to come out of it.
Not being bigger, perhaps you pressed the finger in the scrotum onto the stone at the cut and it came out without difficulty. And know that there may be angles and crevices to some stones so that it is difficult for them to come out.
And among them there are smooth ones that resemble ebony and curved, so it is easy for them to come out. And if any of them have angles and crevices then you should extend the incision a little bit. And if they do not come out in this way then you should grasp them firmly with a grip that has a sharp edge like a file.
So that it is secure on the stone and does not slip away. Or you insert into underneath it a delicate instrument with a guarded edge. And if you are unable to do so then extend the incision slightly. And if something of blood obstructs you, then cut it off with forceps.
And if there are more than one, then push the big one first into the bladder's mouth, then cut on it, then push the small ones afterwards. And you do likewise if there are more than two. And if they are very large indeed, then it is ignorance to cut a large incision on them because it exposes to danger one of two things.
Either he will die or a constant dripping of urine will occur in order that the place will not adhere at all; but try to push it until it comes out, or turn it with calabashes until it comes out for sure.
If you have finished your work, wash the wound with a kneading cloth and two cloths that are soft and strong, tie it tight, then pour a wet poultice of oil or drink on roses and cold water over it to calm the hot swelling; then let the patient lie down on his back without removing the bandage until the third day.
If it has healed, wash the area with a lot of water and oil, then treat it with Al-Nakhli ointment and Al-Basiliqun ointment until it clears up; if there is an excess of hot swelling, coagulation, or something like that, such as blood freezing in the bladder and urine refusing to come out, this can be known from the blood coming out with the urine.
Then insert your finger into the wound and bring out that blood; for if it remains, it will invite badness of the bladder and its abscessing. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water and salt, and apply each type of treatment which agrees with what it has been treated with until it heals.
And at all times of treatment, it is necessary to bind the thighs together and tie them up so that the remedies placed on the place may be fixed; if the stone was small and entered the urethra and the urine refused to come out, then treat it with what I have described before that it does not reach the cut.
Often I have been satisfied with this treatment without making an incision, having tried that; it is to take a rod of iron like this:.
Like a triangle-shaped end with an edge on the rod, then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it does not go back to the bladder; then insert the iron rod into the urethra gently until the rod reaches the same stone.
You should hold the catheter with your hand in the urethra a little at a time, as you try to puncture it until it is perforated on the other side.
